Conflicting Witnesses in Zina: No Hadd Applied
Ruling on conflicting testimonies of zina from two groups of four witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when two groups of four witnesses testify to zina at the same time in different places, and explain why no hadd is applied to either the accused or the witnesses.

Core Idea
If two groups of four witness a single zina in two places simultaneously, both testimonies are rejected due to certain falsehood of one group, and no hadd applies.

This lesson addresses a unique scenario in Hanafi hudud law: two complete sets of witnesses claim the same couple committed zina at the exact same time in different locations. Since simultaneous zina in two places is impossible, one group must be lying. However, no punishment is inflicted on either the couple or the witnesses. The reasoning hinges on the principle that hudud are averted by doubts (shubahat), even if the doubt is not perfectly strong.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State the main ruling: no hadd on the accused couple and no hadd on any of the eight witnesses.
This is the munafa (conclusion) of the passage.
2
Recognize the rational proof
Understand that the impossibility of one act in two places makes the falsehood of one group certain, and since there is no preponderance, both testimonies are rejected.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) used by the Hanafis.
3
Explain why no hadd on the couple
Because zina is not proven – the rejected testimonies do not establish the act beyond doubt.
Hudud require near-certain proof.
4
Explain why no hadd on the witnesses
Because there remains a possibility that each group is truthful, creating a shubhah (doubt) that prevents the hadd of qadhf.
The text discusses that even a remote possibility creates a valid shubhah.
5
Evaluate the internal debate on shubhah
Consider the objection that this is only a 'shubhah of shubhah' and should not avert hadd, and then follow the Hanafi response refuting that objection.
This shows the depth of Hanafi usul in hudud cases.

وإن شَهِدَ أربعة بزناه في وقت معين، وأربعة أخرى بزناه في ذلك الوقت في بلد آخر، فلا حد عليهما؛ لأنَّ شهادة أحد الفريقين مردودة؛ لتيقن كذبه، ولا رجحان لأحدهما فيرد الجميع، ولا على الشهود؛ لاحتمال صدق أحد الفريقين. قوله: فلا حد عليهما؛ أي على الرجل والمرأة؛ لأنّ كذب أحد الفريقين متيقن لعدم إمكان صدور فعل واحدٍ من رجل واحد في وقت واحد في مكانين متباعدين، فلم يثبت الزني بشهادة أحدهما. [٢] قوله: ولا رجحان؛ يعني ليس في أحد الفريقين ما يُرجح قبوله على الآخر، وفيه احتراز عما لو لم توجد في أحد الفريقين شرائط قبول الشهادة، ووجدت في الآخر، فحينئذ تقبل شهادة الفريق المجتمعة لصفات القبول وتردّ شهادة الآخر. [٣] قوله: لاحتمال صدق أحد الفريقين؛ الأولى أن يقول: لاحتمال صدق كلّ من الفريقين، كما في «الهداية». والحاصل: إن صدق كلّ من الفريقين محتمل، وكذب أحدهما لا بعينه متيقن، فلتيقن كذب أحدهما دُرِءَ الحد عن الرَّجل والمرأة، ولاحتمال صدق كلِّ منهما دُرِءَ الحد عن الشهود الثمانية؛ لأنَّ حد القذف إنّما يقام إذا لم يثبت الزنا ولم توجد شبهة، وهاهنا شبهة الزنا قائمة لاحتمال صدق الشهود. فإن قلت: كيف يجتمع احتمال صدق كل منهما مع تيقن كذب أحدهما، بل لا يكون هاهنا إلا احتمال صدق أحدهما. قلت: تيقن الكذب متعلق بأحدهما لا بعينه، وهو لا يضر في وجود احتمال الصدق في كل منهما على انفراده، وإنّ ما يضر احتمال صدق مجموعهما. ويمكن أن يقال: إن صدق كل منهما وإن كان محتملاً، لكن وجود احتمال الصدق في أحدهما لا بعينه أيضاً كافٍ لدرء الحدّ عن الشهود، فلذلك اكتفى عليه الشارح، فافهم هذا فإنّه مع أكثر ما مرّ وما يأتي في هذا البحث من سوانح الوقت. بعد أن اكتمل نصاب الشهادة في كل واحد من الفريقين عليه: أنه يحتمل أن يكون كلُّ واحدٍ منهما كاذباً، والظاهر هذا لما مرّ من تيقن كذب أحدهما وعدم رجحان أحدهما، فيكون صدق أحدهما محتملاً احتمالاً بعيدا، ثم على تقدير صدق أحدهما يحتمل أن يكونَ الصَّادقُ هذا الفريق المعين أو ذلك الفريق، ففي صدق كل واحد احتمال الاحتمال، وهو شبهة الشبهة، فلا اعتبار لها. فأقول: وإنما لا يحدُّ الشُّهود؛ لوجودِ أربعة شهداء، فشهادة كل فريق إن لم توجب حداً على المشهود عليه، فلا أقل من أن توجب تهمةً. قوله: يرد عليه... الخ؛ إيراد على ما ذكره وجهاً لسقوط الحد عن الشهود، وحاصله: إنه قد مرّ أنّ كذب أحد الفريقين متيقن مع عدم الرجحان، واحتمال كذب كل منهما أيضاً قائم، فاحتمال صدق أحدهما احتمال بعيد، فبعد ذلك مع احتمال صدق أحدهما يحتمل أن يكون الصادق هذا الفريق أو الفريق الآخر، فيكون في صدق كل منهما احتمال الاحتمال، ومثله لا يعتبر في هذا الباب، فإنّ الحدود إنما تسقط بوجود الشبهة لا بشبهة الشبهة. وأنت تعلم ما في هذا من السخافة؛ وذلك لأنّ احتمال كذب كل منهما منفي بالشرع؛ لأنه جعل الشارع صدق الشاهد العدل في حكم المقطوع به، ولم يعتبر احتمال كذبه، وإنما عرض فيما نحن فيه تيقن كذب أحدهما لعارض، فلا يزيل ذلك قطع الصدق في أحدهما، وإنما يصير شبهة في التعيين، فلا توجد شبهة الشبهة على أن قوله: «والظاهر هذا باطل، فإنّ كذب كل منهما ليس بالظاهر بوجه من الوجوه، وما ذكره من الدليل لا يثبته؛ لأنّ تيقن كذب أحدهما مع عدم الرجحان لا يثبت كون كذب كل منهما ظاهراً. قوله: فأقول... الخ؛ تقرير لسقوط الحد عن الفريقين بوجه آخر، بحيث لا يرد عليه شيء، وحاصله: إنّه قد وُجِدَ نصاب الشهادة هاهنا في كل جانب، فشهادة كلّ فريق توجب تهمة الزنا، وبوجودِ التهمة يندفع حد القذف عن الفريق الآخر. قوله: فلا أقل من... الخ؛ أورد عليه: بأن إيجاب التهمة فرع احتمال الاحتمال، وقد أسقطه عن درجة الاعتبار. وأجيب عنه: بأن احتمال الاحتمال في صدق معيّن، لكن صدق أحد الفريقين هو الاحتمال، ويكفي للتهمة ذلك.
If four [witnesses] testify to his zina at a specific time, and another four testify to his zina at that same time in another town, then there is no hadd upon them [the couple]; because the testimony of one of the two groups is rejected due to certainty of its falsehood, and there is no preponderance of one over the other, so all are rejected. And there is no [hadd] upon the witnesses due to the possibility of truth of one of the two groups. His statement: 'no hadd upon them' means upon the man and the woman; because the falsehood of one of the two groups is certain due to the impossibility of a single act from one man at one time in two distant places, so zina is not established by the testimony of either. [2] His statement: 'no preponderance' means there is nothing in one of the two groups that would give preponderance for acceptance over the other. In this there is a caveat for the case where the conditions for acceptance of testimony are not found in one group and are found in the other—then the testimony of the group possessing the qualities of acceptance is accepted and the testimony of the other is rejected. [3] His statement: 'due to possibility of truth of one of the two groups'—it would be better to say: 'due to the possibility of truth of each of the two groups', as in al-Hidayah. The conclusion: The truth of each of the two groups is possible, and the falsehood of one of them specifically is certain. Due to the certainty of falsehood of one, the hadd from the man and woman is averted; and due to the possibility of truth of each, the hadd from the eight witnesses is averted. Because the hadd of qadhf is only established when zina is not proven and there is no shubhah; here the shubhah of zina exists due to the possibility of truth of the witnesses. If you say: How can the possibility of truth of each coexist with the certainty of falsehood of one? Rather there is only possibility of truth of one here. I say: Certainty of falsehood pertains to one of them not specified, and that does not harm the existence of possibility of truth in each individually; rather what would harm is the possibility of truth of both together. It can also be said: Even though truth of each is possible, the existence of possibility of truth in one of them not specifically is sufficient to avert the hadd from the witnesses, so the commentator sufficed with that. Understand this, for it is along with most of what passed and will come in this research of the exigencies of the time. After the number of witnesses was completed in each of the two groups, there is an objection against it: that it is possible that each of them is lying, and this is apparent due to the certainty of falsehood of one and the lack of preponderance of one, so truth of one is a remote possibility. Then assuming truth of one, it is possible that the truthful one is this specific group or that group, so there is in the truth of each the possibility of possibility, which is shubhah of shubhah, so it is not considered. So I say: The witnesses are not punished [with hadd] because four witnesses exist; the testimony of each group—if it does not necessitate hadd upon the accused, then at least it necessitates suspicion. His statement: 'It is objected... etc.' is an objection to what he mentioned as a reason for dropping the hadd from the witnesses. Its summary: It has passed that the falsehood of one of the two groups is certain along with lack of preponderance, and the possibility of falsehood of each also stands, so the possibility of truth of one is a remote possibility. Then after that, with the possibility of truth of one, it is possible that the truthful one is this group or that group, so in the truth of each there is possibility of possibility, and the like is not considered in this chapter; hudud are only dropped by existence of shubhah, not by shubhah of shubhah. And you know the flimsiness in this; because the possibility of falsehood of each is negated by the Shari'ah, since the Lawgiver has made the truth of a just witness as a definitive matter, and He did not consider the possibility of his falsehood. What occurred here is certainty of falsehood of one due to an accidental factor, so that does not remove the definitive truth from one; rather it becomes a shubhah in determination, so shubhah of shubhah does not exist. Moreover, his statement: 'this is apparent' is false; certainly falsehood of each is not apparent in any way, and what he mentioned as proof does not establish it; because certainty of falsehood of one along with lack of preponderance does not establish that falsehood of each is apparent. His statement: 'So I say... etc.' is a formulation for dropping the hadd from the two groups in another way such that nothing is objected against it. Its summary: The number [of witnesses] here has been completed on each side, so the testimony of each group necessitates a suspicion of zina, and by the existence of suspicion, the hadd of qadhf is repelled from the other group. His statement: 'at least it necessitates... etc.' it is objected: that establishing suspicion is a branch of possibility of possibility, and he has nullified it from the level of consideration. It is answered: that possibility of possibility is in a specific truth, but the truth of one of the two groups is the possibility, and that suffices for suspicion.
Source pages p. 210

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from the chapter of hudud concerning a scenario where two groups of four witnesses each come forward to testify that a specific couple committed zina at the same time but in two different locations. The ruling states that no hadd (prescribed punishment) is applied to the accused couple, nor to any of the eight witnesses. The reasoning is based on the impossibility of the same act occurring in two places simultaneously, which makes the falsehood of one group certain without preponderance. Since we do not know which group is lying, both testimonies are rejected. The couple therefore cannot be punished because zina is not proven. The witnesses are not punished for qadhf (false accusation) because there remains a possibility that one group is truthful; this possibility creates a shubhah (doubt) that prevents the hadd of qadhf. The text then engages with a secondary argument: some might say that since falsehood of one group is certain, and truth of each is only a possibility of a possibility, this should not be considered a valid shubhah. The commentator refutes this by explaining that the Shari'ah presumes a just witness to be truthful, and the only issue here is uncertainty about which group is lying, not about the inherent truthfulness of each. Thus, the possibility of truth in each individual witness remains, and that is sufficient to create a shubhah. The final point is that the existence of four witnesses on each side creates a strong suspicion of zina, which in turn repels the hadd of qadhf from the other group. This lesson illustrates the principle that hudud are averted by doubts (shubahat) and that the threshold for shubhah is not extremely high.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or ambiguity that prevents the application of a hadd punishment. In this context, the possibility that one group of witnesses is truthful creates a shubhah that averts the hadd of qadhf from the witnesses.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment for false accusation of zina. It is applied when zina is not proven and there is no shubhah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why are the eight witnesses not punished with hadd al-qadhf in the scenario of conflicting testimonies?
A) Because they are minors.
B) Because there is a possibility that each group is truthful, creating a shubhah.
C) Because the accused couple retracted their accusation.
D) Because the witnesses are all just.

Key Takeaway
When conflicting testimonies create a shubhah, hudud are averted; the possibility of truth suffices to prevent hadd al-qadhf.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties
intermediate
8 min
Conflicting Zina Testimony and the Role of Shubuha in Averting Hudud
Commentary on conflicting zina testimony and shubuha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school drops both hadd punishments when two groups of four witnesses give conflicting testimony in a zina case, and distinguish between valid shubha and 'shubha of shubha'.

Core Idea
Conflicting testimony from full groups creates shubha that averts both hadd al-zina and hadd al-qadhf.

This passage addresses a complex scenario: two groups of four witnesses each testify that a person committed zina, but we know with certainty that one group is lying. The Hanafi school rules that the accused is not punished for zina, and the witnesses are not punished for qadhf (false accusation). The key is the principle that hudud are averted by shubha (doubt). But what kind of doubt? The objection that this is merely a 'shubha of a shubha' is refuted by the commentator, who shows that the certainty of one group's lying does not negate the Shari'ah's presumption of truthfulness for each witness; it only creates a doubt about which group is truthful. This doubt is sufficient to avert the hadd. The passage also extends the ruling to cases where witnesses are fasiq (sinful) and where a woman's testimony of virginity creates shubha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Two complete groups of four witnesses each testify to zina, but one group is certainly lying. The Hanafi ruling is that both the hadd of zina (on the accused) and the hadd of qadhf (on the witnesses) are dropped.
This is the core of the lesson.
2
Understand the objection: 'shubha of shubha'
An objector argues that since the truthfulness of each group is only a possibility of a possibility (because we know one is lying, and we don't know which), this is a 'shubha of a shubha' and should not be legally considered.
The objector claims that hudud are not averted by such remote doubt.
3
Analyze the Hanafi refutation
The commentator refutes that the Shari'ah presumes the truthfulness of a just witness as definitive. The certainty of one group's lying only creates a doubt about which group is truthful, not a doubt about the truthfulness of witnesses in general. Thus, it is a direct shubha, not a shubha of a shubha.
The principle: the Lawgiver considers a just witness's statement as if certain, until a specific contingency arises.
4
Examine the alternative justification (tuhma)
Even if one rejects the above, the testimony of each group creates at least a suspicion (tuhma) of zina, and that suspicion suffices to drop the hadd of qadhf from the other group. This is a second, independent justification.
Tuhma is a valid basis for shubha in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply to fasiq witnesses and note cross-madhhab dispute
If the witnesses are fasiq, the Hanafi school still considers them eligible to testify. Their testimony creates shubha both for zina (due to the testimony) and against it (due to the deficiency in their performance), so both hudud are dropped. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees because he considers fasiq witnesses invalid.
The practical difference: in the Hanafi school, both hudud are dropped; in the Shafi'i school, the testimony is rejected entirely, which may lead to different consequences.

Source Text

كتاب الحدود باب شهادة الزنا والرجوع عنها

عليه : أنه يحتمل أن يكون كلُّ واحدٍ منهما كاذباً ، والظاهر هذا لما مرّ من تيقن كذب أحدهما وعدم رجحان أحدهما ، فيكون صدق أحدهما محتملاً احتمالاً بعيدا، ثم على تقدير صدق أحدهما يحتمل أن يكونَ الصَّادقُ هذا الفريق المعين أو ذلك الفريق، ففي صدق كل واحد احتمال الاحتمال ، وهو شبهةً الشبهة ، فلا اعتبار لها. فأقول : وإنما لا يحدُّ الشُّهود ؛ لوجودِ أربعة شهداء، فشهادة كل فريق إن لم توجب حداً على المشهود عليه ، فلا أقل من أن توجب تهمةً [١] قوله : يرد عليه... الخ ؛ إيراد على ما ذكره وجهاً لسقوط الحد عن الشهود، وحاصله : إنه قد مرّ أنّ كذب أحد الفريقين متيقن مع عدم الرجحان، واحتمال كذب كل منهما أيضاً قائم، فاحتمال صدق أحدهما احتمال بعيد ، ذلك فبعد احتمال ومع صدق أحدهما يحتمل أن يكون الصادق هذا الفريق أو الفريق الآخر، فيكون في صدق كل منهما احتمال الاحتمال ، ومثله لا يعتبر في هذا الباب، فإنّ الحدود إنما تسقط بوجود الشبهة لا بشبهة الشبهة.
وأنت تعلم ما في هذا من السخافة ؛ وذلك لأنّ احتمال كذب كل منهما منفي بالشرع ؛ لأنه جعل الشارع صدق الشاهد العدل في حكم المقطوع به، ولم يعتبر احتمال كذبه، وإنما عرض فيما نحن فيه تيقن كذب أحدهما لعارض، فلا يزيل ذلك قطع الصدق في أحدهما، وإنما يصير شبهة في التعيين، فلا توجد شبهة الشبهة على أن قوله : «والظاهر هذا باطل، فإنّ كذب كل منهما ليس بالظاهر بوجه من الوجوه، وما ذكره من الدليل لا يثبته ؛ لأنّ تيقن كذب أحدهما مع عدم الرجحان لا يثبت كون كذب كل منهما ظاهراً.
(٢) قوله : فأقول ... الخ ؛ تقرير لسقوط الحد عن الفريقين بوجه آخر، بحيث لا يرد عليه شيء، وحاصله : إنّه قد وُجِدَ نصاب الشهادة هاهنا في كل جانب، فشهادة كلّ فريق توجب تهمة الزنا، وبوجودِ التهمة يندفع حد القذف عن الفريق الآخر.
[٣] قوله : فلا أقل من... الخ ؛ أورد عليه : بأن إيجاب التهمة فرع احتمال الاحتمال ، وقد أسقطه . عن درجة الاعتبار.
وأجيب عنه : بأن احتمال الاحتمال في صدق معيّن، لكن صدق أحد الفريقين هو الاحتمال، ويكفي للتهمة ذلك.
وإن نظرَتِ امراة واحدة فقالت : هي بكر تثبت بشهادتها البكارة : فيندرى حد الزنا، ولا يثبت حد القذف لشرطيَّةِ الرِّجال". وإذا كانوا فسقةً يندرى الحد ، ولا يحدُّ الشُّهود ؛ لأنَّ الفسقة أهلُ الشَّهادة، فوجدت شهادة الأربعة [١]قوله : يندرئ بها ... الخ ؛ ولدرء الحدّ عن الشهود وجوه أخر أيضاً :
١ . منها : إنّ الظاهر صدق الشهود، والكذب خلاف الظاهر، فيتقدر بقدر الضرورة.
٢. ومنها : إن الثابت بشهادة الفريقين الزنا المطلق، وإقامة حد القذف مشروطة بقذف الزنا المعين، ولم يثبت.
. ومنها : إنه قام الدليلُ المثبت للزنا ذاتاً ، وإنما امتنع ثبوته لعارض فأورث ذلك شبهة سَقَطَ الحد بها عنهم.
[٢]قوله : وإن نظرت ... الخ ؛ يعني شهدوا بأنه زنى بفلانة، فنظرت امرأة تلك المزنية، وقالت : هي باكرة فحينئذ يسقط الحد عنهما ؛ لوجود الشبهة، فإنّ البكارة لا تجتمع مع الزنى، وقولُ المرأة الواحدة حجة في هذا الباب.
[٣] قوله : الشرطية الرجال ؛ يعني تشترط في ثبوت القذف الموجب للحدّ شهادة الرجال، وهاهنا البكارة تثبت بقول النساء.
[٤] قوله : أهل الشهادة ... الخ ؛ قال في «الهداية»: «لأنَّ الفاسق من أهل الأداء والتحمّل، وإن كان في أدائه نوعُ قصور لتهمة الفسق ، ولهذا لو قضى القاضي بشهادة فاسق ينفذ عندنا ، فيثبت بشهادتهم شبهة الزنا، وباعتبار قصور في الأداء لتهمة الفسق يثبت شبهة عدم الزنا، فلهذا امتنع الحدان، وسيأتي فيه خلاف الشافعي له بناء على أصله إنّ الفاسق ليس من أهل الشهادة، فهو كالعبد عنده).
Book of Hudud, Chapter on Testimony of Zina and Retraction Therefrom. Upon it: that it is possible that each one of them is a liar, and the apparent is this because of what passed of certainty of the lying of one of them and absence of preponderance of one of them, so the truthfulness of one of them is a remote possibility. Then on the assumption of truthfulness of one of them, it is possible that the truthful one is this specific group or that group, so in the truthfulness of each one there is a possibility of a possibility, and this is a shubha of a shubha, so it is not considered. So I say: And the witnesses are not punished only because of the existence of four witnesses, so the testimony of each group, if it does not necessitate a hadd upon the one testified against, then at least it necessitates suspicion. [1] His saying: 'It is objected upon... etc.': An objection to what he mentioned as a justification for dropping the hadd from the witnesses. Its summary: It has passed that the lying of one of the two groups is certain with absence of preponderance, and the possibility of lying of each of them also exists, so the possibility of truthfulness of one of them is a remote possibility. Then after possibility and with truthfulness of one of them, it is possible that the truthful one is this group or the other group, so in the truthfulness of each one there is a possibility of a possibility, and the like of this is not considered in this chapter, for hudud are only dropped by the existence of shubha, not by a shubha of a shubha. And you know what is in this of foolishness; and that is because the possibility of lying of each of them is negated by the Shari'ah, because the Lawgiver has made the truthfulness of the just witness in the ruling of something definitively established, and did not consider the possibility of his lying. Only in our case has the certainty of lying of one of them occurred due to a contingency, so that does not remove the definitive truthfulness in one of them, but it becomes a shubha in specification, so a shubha of a shubha does not exist. Moreover, his saying: 'And the apparent is this' is false, for the lying of each of them is not apparent in any way, and what he mentioned of the proof does not establish it, because certainty of lying of one of them with absence of preponderance does not prove that the lying of each of them is apparent. (2) His saying: 'So I say... etc.': A statement for dropping the hadd from the two groups in another way, such that nothing is objected against it. Its summary: that the required number of witnesses (nisab) has been found here on each side, so the testimony of each group necessitates suspicion of zina, and by the existence of suspicion, the hadd of qadhf is repelled from the other group. [3] His saying: 'Then at least... etc.': It was objected against it: that necessitating suspicion is a branch of possibility of possibility, and he has removed it from the degree of consideration. And it was answered: that possibility of possibility is in the truthfulness of a specific one, but the truthfulness of one of the two groups is the possibility, and that suffices for suspicion. And if one woman looked and said: 'She is a virgin', her testimony establishes virginity, so the hadd of zina is averted, and the hadd of qadhf is not established because of the condition of men. And if they (the witnesses) are sinful (fasiq), the hadd is averted, and the witnesses are not punished, because sinful people are people of testimony, so the testimony of four is found. [1] His saying: 'It is averted by it... etc.': And for averting the hadd from the witnesses there are also other aspects: 1. Among them: that the apparent is the truthfulness of the witnesses, and lying is contrary to the apparent, so it is limited to the extent of necessity. 2. Among them: that what is established by the testimony of the two groups is absolute zina, and establishment of the hadd of qadhf is conditional upon accusing specific zina, and it is not established. 3. Among them: that the proof establishing zina in essence has been presented, but its establishment is prevented by a contingency, so that gives rise to a shubha by which the hadd is dropped from them. [2] His saying: 'And if she looked... etc.': meaning they testified that he committed zina with so-and-so, then a woman looked at that alleged adulteress and said: 'She is a virgin', then at that moment the hadd drops from both of them due to the existence of shubha, for virginity does not coincide with zina, and the word of one woman is a proof in this chapter. [3] His saying: 'The conditionality of men': meaning that for establishing qadhf that necessitates the hadd, the testimony of men is required, and here virginity is established by the words of women. [4] His saying: 'People of testimony... etc.'; he said in al-Hidayah: 'Because the fasiq is among the people of performance and accepting, even though in his performance there is a kind of deficiency due to suspicion of fisq. For this reason, if the judge judges by the testimony of a fasiq, it is executed in our school. So by their testimony a shubha of zina is established, and by considering the deficiency in performance due to suspicion of fisq, a shubha of absence of zina is established, so for this reason the two hudud are prevented. There will come the difference of al-Shafi'i [on this], based on his principle that the fasiq is not among the people of testimony, so he is like a slave according to him.'
Source pages p. 211

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter of testimony in hudud, specifically addressing the scenario where two groups of witnesses testify to zina but one group is certainly lying. The commentator explains that despite the certainty that one group is lying, the hudud punishments (both for zina and for qadhf) are dropped due to the presence of shubha (doubt). The core principle is that hudud are averted by shubha, but not by a 'shubha of a shubha' (a remote doubt). The objector claims that since the truthfulness of each group is merely a possibility of a possibility, it should not count as shubha. The commentator refutes this by stating that Shari'ah presumes the truthfulness of just witnesses until proven otherwise; the certainty of one group's lying only creates uncertainty about which group is truthful, which is sufficient shubha. The passage then presents alternative justifications: (1) the witnesses are presumed truthful, (2) absolute zina is established but specific zina needed for qadhf is not, and (3) a contingency prevents full proof, creating shubha. It also discusses a case where a woman's testimony about virginity creates shubha, dropping the hadd of zina. Finally, the passage addresses witnesses who are fasiq (sinful): according to the Hanafi school, a fasiq is still a valid witness, so their testimony creates shubha on both sides (zina and no zina), thus both hudud are dropped. The commentator notes that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees because he holds fasiq witnesses as invalid, but this passage clarifies the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
شبهة (shubha): A doubt or uncertainty that prevents the application of hadd punishments.
شبهة الشبهة (shubhat al-shubha): A remote doubt that is not legally considered sufficient to avert hadd.
تهمة (tuhma): Suspicion; in this context, the suspicion of zina arising from testimony, sufficient to drop the hadd of qadhf.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for false accusation of zina (eighty lashes).
بكارة (bikara): Virginity; a woman's testimony of virginity creates shubha that averted hadd of zina.
فسقة (fasaqa): Sinful witnesses; in Hanafi fiqh, eligible for testimony with some deficiency.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why are the witnesses in the case of two conflicting groups of four witnesses not punished for qadhf?
A) Because both groups are truthful.
B) Because the testimony of each group creates a suspicion (tuhma) that averts the hadd.
C) Because the witnesses are all fasiq and thus their testimony is invalid.
D) Because the number of witnesses is insufficient.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when two full groups of witnesses present conflicting testimony in a zina case, the uncertainty created is a valid shubha that drops both the hadd of zina and the hadd of qadhf.

Three Rational Grounds for Warding Off Hadd from Witnesses
Commentary providing three rational justifications for warding off hadd from witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three rational grounds for warding off the hadd punishment from witnesses in a zina case and explain how each ground creates a shubhah sufficient to drop the punishment.

Core Idea
Hadd is warded off from witnesses by any one of three rational shubahat: default truthfulness, lack of specific accusation, or evidentiary obstacle.

In Hanafi criminal law, the principle is that punishments are suspended by doubts. This passage, from a commentary on Al-Wiqayah, provides three specific rational arguments that justify dropping the hadd from witnesses who testify to zina but whose testimony is somehow questionable. These arguments are based on legal reasoning (ta'lil) rather than explicit textual proof, illustrating how the Hanafi school applies the maxim 'yundari'u al-hadd bi al-shubahat' (the hadd is warded off by doubts). Understanding these arguments deepens your appreciation of the Hanafi method of juristic reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Contextualise the Passage
Recognise that this passage is a commentary on the principle that when witnesses testify to zina, the hadd punishment (stoning or lashing) may be warded off from the witnesses themselves if a shubhah (doubt) arises. The commentator lists three rational justifications.
The 'other party' mentioned refers to the witnesses or the accused? Context: the default ruling is that false witnesses receive the hadd of qadhf; here the commentators explain exceptions.
2
Identify the First Reason: Default Truthfulness
The first argument: witnesses are presumed truthful (al-zahir sidquhum). Falsehood is contrary to the apparent, so punishing them for false testimony (the hadd of qadhf) is limited to the extent of necessity – i.e., only when their falsehood is proven beyond doubt.
This is a procedural presumption that protects witnesses from punishment unless clear evidence of lying exists.
3
Identify the Second Reason: Lack of Specific Accusation
The second argument: the testimony of the two parties (the accuser and accused? Or the witnesses?) establishes 'absolute zina' (al-zina al-mutlaq) – an unspecified act. The hadd of qadhf, however, requires an accusation of a specific act of zina (qadhf zina mu'ayyan). Since no specific act is alleged, the condition for qadhf is not met.
This is a strict interpretation of the conditions for qadhf.
4
Identify the Third Reason: Evidentiary Obstacle Creates a Doubt
The third argument: the evidence for the existence of zina in substance (dalil muthbit li al-zina dhatan) is established, but its establishment is prevented by a hindrance (li 'arad). This hindrance creates a shubhah that drops the hadd from the witnesses.
The exact nature of the 'hindrance' is not specified; it could be absence of corroboration or procedural defect.
5
Synthesize: Any One Shubhah Suffices
The three reasons are independent – any one of them is sufficient to ward off the hadd. This reflects the Hanafi principle that punishments are suspended by even a single doubt.
This is not a cumulative requirement; each reason stands alone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يندرى بها الحد عن الفريق الآخر. قوله : يندرئ بها ... الخ ; ولدرء الحدّ عن الشهود وجوه أخر أيضاً : ١ . منها : إنّ الظاهر صدق الشهود، والكذب خلاف الظاهر، فيتقدر بقدر الضرورة. ٢. ومنها : إن الثابت بشهادة الفريقين الزنا المطلق، وإقامة حد القذف مشروطة بقذف الزنا المعين، ولم يثبت. ٣. ومنها : إنه قام الدليلُ المثبت للزنا ذاتاً ، وإنما امتنع ثبوته لعارض فأورث ذلك شبهة سَقَطَ الحد بها عنهم.
The hadd is warded off from the other party. He said: 'Yundari'u biha... etc.' And for warding off the hadd from the witnesses, there are other aspects as well: 1. Among them: That the apparent is the truthfulness of the witnesses, and falsehood is contrary to the apparent, so it is limited to the extent of necessity. 2. Among them: That established by the testimony of the two parties is absolute zina, and the establishment of the hadd of qadhf is conditional upon accusing a specific zina, and it was not established. 3. Among them: That the evidence for the existence of zina in substance is established, but its establishment is prevented due to a hindrance, which gives rise to a doubt by which the hadd is dropped from them.
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This is a commentary on the principle that when witnesses testify to zina, if there is a doubt (shubhah), the hadd punishment is warded off from the witnesses themselves. The commentator provides three rational arguments: (1) The default assumption is that witnesses are truthful; falsehood is exceptional, so the punishment for false testimony is only applied when necessary. (2) The testimony of the two parties (the accuser and the accused?) establishes absolute zina, but the hadd for qadhf requires a specific accusation, which is not present. (3) The evidence for the substance of zina exists, but its establishment is prevented by an obstacle (like the absence of corroboration), creating a doubt that drops the hadd. These arguments are based on legal reasoning (ta'lil) and reflect the Hanafi principle of warding off punishments by doubts.

Key Terms
يندرئ (yundari'u): The passive verb meaning 'is warded off' or 'is repelled', used specifically for the dropping of hadd punishment.
شبهة (shubhah): A doubt or uncertainty that arises from a legal ambiguity, sufficient to prevent the application of hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT one of the three reasons for warding off hadd from witnesses?
A) The apparent truthfulness of witnesses limits punishment to necessity.
B) The testimony establishes absolute zina, not a specific act, so qadhf conditions are unmet.
C) The witnesses did not intend to accuse anyone of zina.
D) Evidence for zina exists but a hindrance prevents its establishment, creating a doubt.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school wards off the hadd of qadhf from witnesses through any one of three rational shubahat, illustrating a penal policy that restricts punishments via broad interpretations of doubt.

Effect of a Woman's Testimony on Virginity in Zina Cases
Explanation of how a woman's testimony on virginity creates shubhah and prevents hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how a single woman's testimony about virginity creates a shubhah that prevents hadd punishments in zina cases, and evaluate the Hanafi position on fasiq testimony in this context.

Core Idea
A single woman's statement of virginity creates a legal doubt that drops the hadd of zina and qadhf.

In this lesson, we examine a scenario from al-Hidayah where witnesses accuse a woman of zina, but a single woman testifies that she is a virgin. The Hanafi school treats this testimony as sufficient to create a shubhah (legal doubt), preventing both the hadd of zina and the hadd of false accusation (qadhf). The passage also addresses why a fasiq (sinful) witness can still create this doubt, contrasting with the Shafi'i position. Understanding this case reveals the Hanafi approach to evidence and the expansion of shubhah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State what happens when witnesses testify to zina and then a single woman says the accused is a virgin. The hadd of zina is dropped from both parties.
Additionally, the witnesses are not subject to hadd of qadhf because qadhf requires male witnesses, and here the evidence of virginity comes from a woman.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof is that virginity (bakarah) and zina cannot coexist (la tajtami'u). The statement of a single woman is accepted as evidence for this physical fact.
This is a rational proof (dalil 'aqli) supported by the fiqh principle that women's testimony is valid for matters only women can know.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
The presence of an intact hymen directly contradicts the occurrence of zina, creating a strong doubt (shubhah) that outweighs the witnesses' testimony.
In Hanafi law, shubhah prevents the application of hadd punishments, which are reserved for cases of absolute certainty.
4
Examine the Fasiq Witness Issue
Even if the testifying woman is a fasiq (sinner), her testimony is still accepted to create shubhah, because she is from ahl al-ada' wa al-tahammul (qualified to give and receive testimony).
The Hanafi view distinguishes between eligibility (ahl al-shahada) and moral integrity ('adalah). A fasiq's deficiency only reduces weight, not validity.
5
Compare with Shafi'i Position
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that a fasiq is not from ahl al-shahada, so his testimony is like that of a slave: rejected entirely.
The practical consequence: under Hanafi law, a fasiq's testimony can prevent hadd; under Shafi'i law, it would be dismissed and hadd might apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[٢] قوله : وإن نظرت ... الخ ; يعني شهدوا بأنه زنى بفلانة، فنظرت امرأة تلك المزنية، وقالت : هي باكرة فحينئذ يسقط الحد عنهما ؛ لوجود الشبهة، فإنّ البكارة لا تجتمع مع الزنى، وقولُ المرأة الواحدة حجة في هذا الباب. [٣] قوله : الشرطية الرجال ; يعني تشترط في ثبوت القذف الموجب للحدّ شهادة الرجال، وهاهنا البكارة تثبت بقول النساء. [٤] قوله : أهل الشهادة ... الخ ; قال في «الهداية»: «لأنَّ الفاسق من أهل الأداء والتحمّل، وإن كان في أدائه نوعُ قصور لتهمة الفسق ، ولهذا لو قضى القاضي بشهادة فاسق ينفذ عندنا ، فيثبت بشهادتهم شبهة الزنا، وباعتبار قصور في الأداء لتهمة الفسق يثبت شبهة عدم الزنا، فلهذا امتنع الحدان، وسيأتي فيه خلاف الشافعي له بناء على أصله إنّ الفاسق ليس من أهل الشهادة، فهو كالعبد عنده). (۱) انتهى من «الهداية» (۵ : ۲۸۹).
[2] He said: 'And if a woman looked... etc.' Meaning that they testified that he committed zina with so-and-so, then a woman looked at that alleged fornicator and said: 'She is a virgin.' At that time, the hadd is dropped from both of them due to the existence of doubt (shubhah), because virginity and zina cannot coexist, and the statement of a single woman is evidence in this chapter. [3] He said: 'The condition of men.' Meaning that for the establishment of qadhf which obligates hadd, the testimony of men is required, and here virginity is established by the statement of women. [4] He said: 'People of testimony... etc.' He said in al-Hidayah: 'Because a fasiq is among the people of performance (ada') and acceptance (tahammul), even though there is a kind of deficiency in his performance due to the suspicion of fisq. For this reason, if a judge passes judgment based on the testimony of a fasiq, it is enforceable according to us. So by their testimony, a doubt (shubhah) of zina is established, and by considering the deficiency in performance due to the suspicion of fisq, a doubt of non-zina is established. Therefore, both hadds are prevented. The difference with al-Shafi'i will come based on his principle that a fasiq is not among the people of testimony, so he is like a slave according to him.' (End from al-Hidayah 5:289).
Source pages p. 212

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on the scenario where witnesses testify to zina, but then a single woman testifies that the accused woman is virgin. The commentator explains that this testimony creates a strong doubt (shubhah) because virginity is incompatible with zina, so the hadd of zina is dropped from both parties. However, the hadd of qadhf is not established against the witnesses, because qadhf requires the testimony of men, and here the evidence of virginity comes from women. The commentator then quotes al-Hidayah regarding the status of fasiq witnesses: they are still eligible to give testimony in the Hanafi school, their testimony is accepted and can create a doubt of zina, but their moral deficiency also creates a doubt that no zina occurred due to the possibility of falsehood. Thus, both hadd punishments are warded off. The passage notes that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees because he holds that a fasiq is not qualified to testify at all, akin to a slave.

Key Terms
بكارة (bakarah): Virginity, specifically the physical state of the hymen being intact, used as evidence against the occurrence of zina.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt that prevents the application of hadd punishments; here it arises from the contradiction between the testimony and visible virginity.
فاسق (fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, thus lacking moral integrity (adalah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The judge ruled that no crime occurred.

Key Takeaway
A single woman's testimony about virginity creates a shubhah that prevents hadd punishments, and even a fasiq's testimony can effect this under Hanafi law.

Testimony upon Testimony (Shahada 'ala al-Shahada) in Zina Cases
Ruling on shahada 'ala al-shahada in zina and the effect of rejection on original witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on shahada 'ala al-shahada in zina cases and explain why the rejection of substitute testimony also bars the original witnesses from testifying in that incident.

Core Idea
In zina, testimony upon testimony is rejected due to heightened doubt; once rejected, it cannot be reintroduced even by the original witnesses.

This passage from the Hidayah commentary addresses a crucial procedural point in hudud cases: when witnesses appear in court as substitutes for the original eyewitnesses, their testimony is not accepted because of the increased risk of error in transmission. The ruling extends further: even if the original witnesses later come forward, their testimony is also barred in that same case. Let us examine the reasoning and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling and its condition
The hadd punishment is not applied when witnesses testify as substitutes (shahada 'ala al-shahada). The condition is that the original witnesses are unable to attend (death, illness, travel), but even then, for zina it is never accepted.
The ruling is procedural, not a hukm taklifi.
2
Understand the rationale: increased doubt
The reason is that when speech is transmitted through tongues, addition and omission tend to occur, creating an increased doubt (shubhah). In hudud, any doubt prevents punishment.
This is a rational proof (dalil aqli).
3
Trace the consequence: original witnesses also barred
If the substitutes' testimony is rejected, the original witnesses cannot later testify in the same incident. The rejection of the substitutes is considered a rejection of the originals from one aspect due to the unity of their testimony.
The principle: once testimony is rejected in a case, it is never accepted again in that incident.
4
Note the qualification: specific to hudud and same incident
The rule does not extend to non-hudud cases (e.g., property disputes) or to different incidents. It is confined to the same case where the rejection occurred.
An objection that this would bar originals in property cases is invalid; the rule is specific to hudud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانوا شهوداً على شهودٍ لم يحدّ ؛ لأنَّ في شهادتهم زيادة شبهة ؛ لأنَّ الكلام إذا تداولته الألسنة يتطرق إليه زيادة ونقصان ، ثُمَّ إن جاءَ الأصول فشهدوا على ذلك الزّنا بعينه بعد شهادة الفروع، لم يحد أيضاً ؛ لأن شهادتهم قد رُدَّت من وجه برد فروعهم، والشهادة إذا ردت مرة في حادثة لا تقبل فيها أبدا [1] قوله : وإن كانوا ; أي الشهود الشاهدون بحضرة الحاكم شهودا على شهود الزنا بأن يقول كلّ منهم : أشهد أنّ فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته هكذا، وقال لي : اشهد على شهادتي بذلك، وهذا عند تعذر حضور الأصول بموت أو مرض أو سفر، فإنّه لا تقبل الشهادة على الشهادة عند قدرة الأصول على أداء الشهادة على ما ثبت تقريره في «كتاب الشهادات». [٢] قوله : لم يحد ; أي الرجلُ ،والمرأة، وكذا لا يحد الشهود لا الفروع ; لأنهم حاكون للقذف، وحكاية القذف ليست بقذف ، وكذا لا يُحَدُّ الأصولُ بالطريق الأولى. [۳] قوله : زيادة شبهة ; هذه الإضافة بيانية ; أي زيادة هي مشبهة، فإنّه لا شبهة في شهادة الأصول حتى يقال : إنّ في شهادة الفروع شبهة زائدة، ويمكن أن يقال: إنّ المراد أنّ في أداء شهادة الفروع عند الحاكم شبهة زائدة، ونفس الشبهة ثبت بإشهادِ الأصول في غير مجلس الحاكم. [٤]قوله : إذا تداولته الألسنة ; بفتح الهمزة وسكون اللام وسكون السين المهملة، اللسان. [0] قوله : يتطرق ; مضارع من التطرق بالفارسية: راه گرفتن، والحاصل : إنّ الكلام الواحد إذا صدر من ألسنة مختلفة وقع فيه شيء من التغير زيادة أو نقصاناً. (٦) قوله : ثم ; أي بعدما شَهِدَ الفروعُ إن حضر الأصول فشهدوا عند الحاكم بذلك الزنا. ا قوله : لان ... الخ ; حاصله : أَنه لَمَّا رُدَّت شهادة الفروع لما مر من وجودِ الشبهة لم تقبل شهادة الأصول بعد ذلك في تلك الواقعة ؛ لأن رد شهادة الفروع ردّ الشهادة الأصول من وجه لاتحاد شهادتهما ، وقد تقرّر في مقره أن الشهادة إذا ردت في حادثة مرة لا تقبل مرّةً أخرى في تلك الحادثة. [۸] قوله : والشهادة ... الخ ; يرد عليه : أنه يستلزم عدم قبول شهادة الأصول في الأموال وغيرها بعدما رُدّت شهادة الفروع لفسقهم ونحو ذلك، وليس كذلك.
And if they (the witnesses) are witnesses upon witnesses, then the hadd is not applied, because in their testimony there is an increased doubt (shubhah). This is because when speech is handled by tongues, addition and omission tend to occur. Then, if the original witnesses (usul) come and testify to that same zina after the testimony of the substitutes (furu'), the hadd is also not applied, because their testimony has been rejected from one aspect by the rejection of their substitutes, and once testimony is rejected in an incident, it is never accepted again therein. [1] He said: 'And if they'; i.e., the witnesses testifying before the judge are witnesses upon witnesses of zina, such that each of them says: 'I bear witness that so-and-so made me witness his testimony thus, and he told me: be a witness upon my testimony.' This is when the presence of the original witnesses is impossible due to death, illness, or travel. Testimony upon testimony is not accepted when the original witnesses are able to perform the testimony themselves, as established in the Book of Testimonies. [2] He said: 'The hadd is not applied'; i.e., neither to the man nor the woman, and likewise the witnesses (the far') are not subjected to hadd because they are merely narrators of the accusation, and narrating an accusation is not itself an accusation. Likewise, the original witnesses (usul) are not subjected to hadd a fortiori. [3] He said: 'Increased doubt'; this is an explanatory addition; i.e., an increase that is a source of doubt. There is no doubt in the testimony of the original witnesses such that it is said that in the testimony of the substitutes there is an increased doubt. It can be said that the intended meaning is that in the performance of the testimony of the substitutes before the judge, there is an increased doubt, and the doubt itself is established by the original witnesses' (usul) appointment in a non-judicial setting. [4] He said: 'When it is handled by tongues'; with fatha on the hamza and sukun on the lam and sukun on the sin, lisān (tongue). [6] He said: 'Yatatarraq'; present tense from al-tatarruq in Persian: 'rāh giriftan' (to take a path). The point: When a single statement originates from different tongues, some change occurs in it, either increase or decrease. (6) He said: 'Then'; i.e., after the substitutes (furu') have testified, if the original witnesses (usul) come and testify before the judge regarding that zina. (a) He said: 'Because... etc.' The summary: When the testimony of the substitutes (furu') was rejected due to the existence of doubt as mentioned, the testimony of the original witnesses (usul) is not accepted afterwards in that incident, because the rejection of the testimony of the substitutes is, from one aspect, a rejection of the testimony of the original witnesses due to the unity of their testimony. And it has been established in its place that testimony once rejected in an incident is never accepted again in that incident. [8] He said: 'And the testimony... etc.' An objection is raised against this: It would lead to the non-acceptance of the testimony of the original witnesses in matters of property and other things after the testimony of the substitutes had been rejected due to their fisq and so on, but that is not the case.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage addresses the scenario where the witnesses testifying in court are not the original eyewitnesses but are substitutes (furu') who testify on the basis of the original witnesses' (usul) testimony. The commentator explains that such testimony upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) is not accepted in zina cases because it introduces an additional doubt: verbal reports are prone to alteration when transmitted. Consequently, the hadd punishment is not applied to the accused. Furthermore, if the original witnesses later come and testify directly after the substitutes' testimony has been rejected, their testimony is also not accepted. This is because the rejection of the substitutes' testimony effectively rejects the testimony of the originals as well, since they are essentially the same evidence. The principle is that once a testimony is rejected in a particular case, it cannot be presented again. The commentator notes a potential objection: this would imply that if a substitute's testimony is rejected due to the substitute's immorality, the original witness's testimony becomes inadmissible even in non-hudud cases like property disputes. But the commentator hints that this is not the case, indicating that the rule is specific to hudud cases. The Hanafi position is that the original witness's testimony is not automatically rejected in other matters.

Key Terms
الشهادة على الشهادة (al-shahadah 'ala al-shahadah): Testimony given by a witness who did not directly see the event but heard it from another witness and is appointed to testify on his behalf.
أصول (usul): Original witnesses who directly witnessed the event and appointed substitutes; their testimony is the foundation.
فروع (furu'): Substitute witnesses who testify on behalf of the original witnesses; their testimony is secondary and subject to additional doubts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is the hadd not applied when witnesses testify upon testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) in a zina case?
A) Because the original witnesses were not present.
B) Because the testimony of substitutes creates an additional doubt due to possible alteration.
C) Because the judge rejected all testimony.
D) Because the accused confessed.

Key Takeaway
Testimony upon testimony in zina cases is never accepted due to the heightened risk of error, and the rejection of substitute testimony prevents the original witnesses from testifying in the same incident.

Ruling on Derivative Testimony in Zina: Rejection Due to Doubt
Ruling on derivative testimony in zina with proof and objection-response

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on derivative testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) in zina cases and explain why both branch and original witnesses escape hadd, applying the principle that doubt repels punishment.

Core Idea
Derivative testimony in zina is rejected due to increased doubt — and this rejection permanently bars the original testimony from the same incident.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya, a commentary on Al-Wiqaya, addresses the evidentiary standard in hudud cases, specifically zina. The Hanafi school holds that testimony based on other witnesses (furu‘) introduces unacceptable uncertainty, so no hadd is imposed. Even if the original witnesses (usul) later testify directly, their testimony is also rejected because a rejected testimony cannot be heard again in the same case. The text then defends this ruling against a logical objection concerning property cases, clarifying that the heightened standard for hudud does not apply to civil matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Locate the passage's opening scenario: witnesses testifying on behalf of others (shuhud 'ala shuhud) in a zina case. The ruling is that such testimony does not lead to hadd (whipping). Note that this applies when the original witnesses are unable to attend.
2
Understand the reason for rejection
The text states the reason is 'ziyadat shubha' (increased doubt) because oral transmission via tongues introduces alteration. Analyze this: the uncertainty inherent in hearsay makes the testimony insufficient for the high certainty required for hudud.
Hanafi principle: hudud are repelled by doubts (al-hudud tudra' bi al-shubuhat).
3
Trace the consequence for original witnesses
The passage then rules that if the original witnesses later appear and testify directly to the same zina, they also escape hadd. The reason is that their testimony was partially rejected by the rejection of their branches, and a rejected testimony cannot be reintroduced in the same case (al-shahada idha ruddat marratan fi haditha la tuqbal fiha abadan).
Note the logical chain: rejection of furu' → implies rejection of usul via the unity of the testimonial 'incident'.
4
Analyze the objection and response
The commentator raises an objection: if this logic were applied universally, original testimony would also be rejected in property cases after branch rejection — but that is not the Hanafi position. The response is that rejection in hudud is due to doubt, which is specific to punishment cases; property matters require different evidentiary rules. Also, an alternative justification (suspicion of spreading lewdness) is considered but not relied upon.
This highlights the Hanafi distinction between hudud and mu'amalat in evidentiary standards.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن كانوا شهوداً على شهودٍ لم يحدّ؛ لأنَّ في شهادتهم زيادة شبهة؛ لأنَّ الكلام إذا تداولته الألسنة يتطرق إليه زيادة ونقصان، ثُمَّ إن جاءَ الأصول فشهدوا على ذلك الزّنا بعينه بعد شهادة الفروع، لم يحد أيضاً؛ لأن شهادتهم قد رُدَّت من وجه برد فروعهم، والشهادة إذا ردت مرة في حادثة لا تقبل فيها أبدا. [1] قوله: وإن كانوا؛ أي الشهود الشاهدون بحضرة الحاكم شهودا على شهود الزنا بأن يقول كلّ منهم: أشهد أنّ فلاناً أشهدني على شهادته هكذا، وقال لي: اشهد على شهادتي بذلك، وهذا عند تعذر حضور الأصول بموت أو مرض أو سفر، فإنّه لا تقبل الشهادة على الشهادة عند قدرة الأصول على أداء الشهادة على ما ثبت تقريره في «كتاب الشهادات». [2] قوله: لم يحد؛ أي الرجلُ، والمرأة، وكذا لا يحد الشهود لا الفروع؛ لأنهم حاكون للقذف، وحكاية القذف ليست بقذف، وكذا لا يُحَدُّ الأصولُ بالطريق الأولى. [3] قوله: زيادة شبهة؛ هذه الإضافة بيانية؛ أي زيادة هي مشبهة، فإنّه لا شبهة في شهادة الأصول حتى يقال: إنّ في شهادة الفروع شبهة زائدة، ويمكن أن يقال: إنّ المراد أنّ في أداء شهادة الفروع عند الحاكم شبهة زائدة، ونفس الشبهة ثبت بإشهادِ الأصول في غير مجلس الحاكم. [4] قوله: إذا تداولته الألسنة؛ بفتح الهمزة وسكون اللام وسكون السين المهملة، اللسان. قوله: يتطرق؛ مضارع من التطرق بالفارسية: راه گرفتن، والحاصل: إنّ الكلام الواحد إذا صدر من ألسنة مختلفة وقع فيه شيء من التغير زيادة أو نقصاناً. [5] قوله: ثم؛ أي بعدما شَهِدَ الفروعُ إن حضر الأصول فشهدوا عند الحاكم بذلك الزنا. [6] قوله: لان ... الخ؛ حاصله: أَنه لَمَّا رُدَّت شهادة الفروع لما مر من وجودِ الشبهة لم تقبل شهادة الأصول بعد ذلك في تلك الواقعة؛ لأن رد شهادة الفروع ردّ الشهادة الأصول من وجه لاتحاد شهادتهما، وقد تقرّر في مقره أن الشهادة إذا ردت في حادثة مرة لا تقبل مرّةً أخرى في تلك الحادثة. [7] قوله: والشهادة ... الخ؛ يرد عليه: أنه يستلزم عدم قبول شهادة الأصول في الأموال وغيرها بعدما رُدّت شهادة الفروع لفسقهم ونحو ذلك، وليس كذلك.  وإن شهدوا عمياناً [8] وهذا ضعيف، لأن رد شهادتهم لمعنى يختص بها لا يسري إلى الأصول؛ لعدم ذلك المعنى في شهادتهم. ويمكن أن يقال: إنما تردُّ شهادة الأصول لأنهم سعوا إلى إثباتِ الزِّنا بأمرٍ غير مشروع، فلا تكون شهادتهم حسبة الله تعالى، بل سعياً إلى إشاعة الفاحشة لعداوة أو نحوها، فتردُّ شهادتهم؛ لهذه التهمة. (وإن شهدوا عمياناً وأجيب عنه: بأنّ ردّ شهادة الفروع ليس ردّاً لشهادة الفروع حقيقة بل شبهة، فيعتبر في باب الحدود التي تندرئ بالشبهات لا في باب الأموال وغيرها.
And if they are witnesses upon witnesses, they are not whipped because in their testimony there is increased doubt, because when speech is passed between tongues, increase and decrease enter it. Then if the original witnesses come and testify to that same zina after the branch testimony, they are also not whipped because their testimony has been rejected in some respect by the rejection of their branches, and testimony once rejected in an incident is never accepted in it again. [1] He said: 'And if they are'—i.e., the witnesses testifying in the presence of the judge as witnesses upon witnesses of zina, by each saying: 'I testify that so-and-so made me a witness to his testimony thus, and said to me: be a witness on my testimony to that,' and this when the attendance of the original witnesses is hindered by death, illness, or travel, for testimony upon testimony is not accepted when the original witnesses are able to testify, as established in the Book of Testimonies. [2] He said: 'they are not whipped'—i.e., the man and the woman, and likewise the witnesses are not whipped, neither the branches because they are relating the accusation, and relating accusation is not accusation, and likewise the original witnesses are not whipped a fortiori. [3] He said: 'increased doubt'—this addition is explicative, i.e., an increase that is doubtful, for there is no doubt in the testimony of the original witnesses such that it could be said that in the branch testimony there is added doubt; and it can be said that the meaning is that in the performance of branch testimony before the judge there is added doubt, and the doubt itself is established by the original witnesses' testimonial appointment outside the judge's court. [4] He said: 'when speech is passed between tongues'—with fatha on the hamza and sukun on the lam and sin, 'the tongue.' [5] He said: 'then'—i.e., after the branches have testified, if the original witnesses attend and testify before the judge to that zina. [6] He said: 'because...'—the summary: when the branch testimony was rejected due to the existence of doubt as mentioned, the original testimony is not accepted afterwards in that incident, because the rejection of branch testimony is in some respect a rejection of the original testimony due to the unity of their testimony, and it has been established in its place that testimony once rejected in an incident is not accepted again in that incident. [7] He said: 'and testimony...'—an objection is raised against it: that it entails non-acceptance of original witnesses' testimony in property and other matters after the branch testimony has been rejected due to their corruption and the like, and this is not the case. [PAGE_214] And if they testify while blind [8] this is weak, because rejection of their testimony is due to a meaning specific to them, which does not extend to the original witnesses due to the absence of that meaning in their testimony. And it can be said: the original witnesses' testimony is rejected only because they sought to establish zina by an illegitimate means, so their testimony is not for the sake of Allah, but rather seeking to spread lewdness due to enmity or the like, so their testimony is rejected for this suspicion. (And if they testify while blind) and it is answered: that rejection of branch testimony is not a rejection of branch testimony in reality but due to doubt, so it is considered in the chapter of hudud which are repelled by doubts, not in the chapter of property and other matters.
Source pages p. 213

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on derivative testimony (shahada 'ala al-shahada) in zina cases. The matn states: if witnesses testify based on the testimony of others (furu'), they are not subject to hadd because of increased doubt from oral transmission. Even if the original witnesses (usul) later testify directly, they are also not hadded because the rejection of the furu' testimony partially rejects the usul's testimony, and testimony once rejected in a case is never accepted again in that same case. The sharh clarifies that furu' witnesses merely report the accusation and are not guilty of qadhf, and the usul are also exempt a fortiori. The doubt is explained as a consequence of speech being transmitted across tongues, inevitably altering it. An objection is raised: this reasoning would also reject usul testimony in property cases after furu' were rejected for fasiq, which is not the case. The answer: the rejection of furu' testimony in hadd is due to doubt, not a substantive rejection, so it only applies in hadd cases (which are repelled by doubts) and not in property cases. The alternative justification (suspicion of spreading lewdness) is also considered but found to imply similar consequences in property. The relied-upon position is that the original testimony is not accepted because the rejection of branch testimony, though based on doubt, constitutes a rejection of testimony in that incident, and a rejected testimony cannot be reintroduced. This is specific to hadd because of the principle of repelling punishments by doubts.

Key Terms
شهود على شهود (shuhūd 'alā shuhūd): Witnesses who testify based on the testimony of others (furu'), i.e., derivative testimony.
زيادة شبهة (ziyādat shubha): Increased doubt that exists in branch testimony due to oral transmission, making it insufficient for hadd.
رد الشهادة (radd al-shahāda): Rejection of testimony; once rejected in a case, it cannot be repeated for that same case.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because the original witnesses were absent from court
B) Because testimony once rejected in an incident cannot be accepted again
C) Because they committed qadhf
D) Because they had a personal enmity

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects derivative testimony in zina because oral transmission creates doubt, and this rejection is permanent for that incident even if original witnesses later appear.

Ruling on Ineligible Witnesses in Zina
Ruling when zina witnesses lack eligibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a zina witness lacks legal eligibility, list the categories of ineligible witnesses, and apply the ruling consistently.

Core Idea
If a witness to zina is ineligible, the accused goes free and the witness is hadded for qadhf.

This passage from the Hanafi fiqh text clarifies a critical rule in hudud: not every accusation of zina can be prosecuted—only those brought by eligible witnesses. When witnesses lack the legal capacity (ahliyya) to testify, their accusation becomes a crime itself. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its categories.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is testimony to zina by a person who lacks legal eligibility. The ruling: the accused is not punished, and the witness is subjected to hadd for false accusation (qadhf).
2
List the ineligible categories
The passage mentions: blind person, one who has been hadded for qadhf, slave, insane person, disbeliever, and the like. These all lack ahliyya for testimony in zina cases.
The list is not exhaustive; any person lacking the required probity or capacity is ineligible.
3
Apply the ruling to each category
For each ineligible witness, the same consequence applies: the accused is not hadded, and the witness is hadded for qadhf.
This holds whether all witnesses are ineligible or only some.
4
Understand the generality
The ruling is general: it applies when every witness is ineligible and when some witnesses are ineligible. The testimony as a whole is invalid, and the ineligible witnesses themselves are punished.
Eligible witnesses present alongside ineligible ones are not automatically hadded, but their testimony becomes ineffective.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن شهدوا عمياناً [٤] قوله: وإن شهدوا... الخ؛ حاصل هذه الصور أنه إذا شهد بالزنا من لا أهلية له للشهادة كالأعمى والمحدودِ في القذف والعبد والمجنون والكافر ونحو ذلك لم يحد المشهود عليه؛ لأنه لا تثبت بشهادتهم المال، فكيف يثبت بها الحد فانقلبت شهادتهم قذفاً، فيقام عليهم الحد، وهذا الحكم عام فيما إذا كان كل شاهد ممن لا أهل له، وفيما إذا كان بعض الشهداء ممن لا أهل له.
And if they testify while blind [4] He said: 'And if they testify...' the summary of these cases is that if one who lacks eligibility for testimony testifies to zina, such as a blind person, one who has been hadded for qadhf, a slave, an insane person, a disbeliever, and the like, the accused is not whipped because property is not established by their testimony, so how can hadd be established by it? So their testimony turns into qadhf, so they (the witnesses) are subjected to hadd (of qadhf). This ruling is general whether every witness is ineligible or some of the witnesses are ineligible.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage states the ruling when witnesses to zina are legally ineligible (e.g., blind, previously convicted of qadhf, slave, insane, disbeliever). Their testimony cannot prove zina for hadd, just as it cannot prove property rights. Consequently, their accusation becomes qadhf (false accusation of zina), and they themselves become liable for the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). This applies regardless of whether all or only some of the witnesses are ineligible. The reasoning is qiyas jaliy (obvious analogy): if such witnesses are not credible for property cases, they are even less credible for hadd cases, which require higher certainty. Therefore, the testimony is invalid and treated as an unsubstantiated accusation.

Key Terms
الأعمى (al-a'mā): A blind person; cited as an example of someone lacking eligibility to testify in zina cases.
المحدود في القذف (al-mahdūd fī al-qadhf): A person who has already received the hadd for false accusation of zina; they are considered ineligible witnesses.
انقلبت شهادتهم قذفاً (inqalabat shahādatuhum qadhfan): The testimony is transformed into an accusation of qadhf, subjecting the witnesses to the hadd for false accusation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The slave is accepted as a witness but cannot be punished
B) The accused is whipped, and the slave is not punished
C) The accused is not whipped, and the slave is hadded for qadhf
D) Both the accused and the slave are whipped

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a witness to zina who lacks legal eligibility (e.g., blind, slave, etc.) cannot establish the hadd penalty, and such witnesses become liable for hadd al-qadhf.

The Qiyas Jaliy Argument for Ineligibility
The qiyas jaliy reasoning for rejecting ineligible witnesses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the components of the qiyas jaliy used in this passage and apply it to analogous cases.

Core Idea
If ineligible witnesses cannot establish property rights, then they certainly cannot establish hadd punishment.

The passage uses a powerful analogy (qiyas jaliy) to justify why ineligible witnesses cannot prove zina. The reasoning is: if such witnesses are not accepted for property cases, they are even less acceptable for hudud, which require higher evidentiary standards. This lesson breaks down the logical structure and demonstrates how qiyas works in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original case (asl)
The asl is the testimony of ineligible witnesses in property cases. The ruling there is that their testimony is rejected.
Property cases have relatively lower evidentiary requirements than hudud.
2
Identify the new case (far')
The far' is the testimony of ineligible witnesses in zina cases (hadd).
Hadd cases require the highest level of certainty.
3
Determine the effective cause (illa)
The illa is the lack of legal eligibility (ahliyya) for testimony. This is common to both cases.
The illa is jaliyy (obvious) because the witness's inability to provide credible testimony is clear.
4
Derive the ruling for the new case
Since the illa is the same, the ruling from the asl is transferred: the testimony is invalid. However, in zina cases, the additional consequence is that the witnesses are hadded for qadhf.
The passage adds an a fortiori (awla) reasoning: if the testimony fails in property cases, it is even more deficient in hudud.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

So their testimony turns into qadhf, so they (the witnesses) are subjected to hadd (of qadhf). This ruling is general whether every witness is ineligible or some of the witnesses are ineligible.

Commentary
This passage states the ruling when witnesses to zina are legally ineligible (e.g., blind, previously convicted of qadhf, slave, insane, disbeliever). Their testimony cannot prove zina for hadd, just as it cannot prove property rights. Consequently, their accusation becomes qadhf (false accusation of zina), and they themselves become liable for the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes). Therefore, the testimony is invalid and treated as an unsubstantiated accusation.

Key Terms
قياس جلي (qiyās jalī): Obvious analogy; a form of qiyas where the effective cause (illa) is clearly perceptible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the qiyas jaliy of this passage, what is the effective cause (illa) for rejecting testimony?
A) The type of case (property vs. hudud)
B) The fact that the witnesses are lying
C) The lack of legal eligibility (ahliyya) for testimony
D) The number of witnesses

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school uses qiyas jaliy to extend the rule of ineligibility from property cases to hadd cases, with the illa being the witness's lack of legal capacity.

Witnesses for Zina: Capacity and Number Requirements
Commentary on ruling rejecting testimony of incapable witnesses in zina cases

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witnesses who lack capacity or insufficient number in zina cases and apply Surah an-Nur verse 4 to derive the hadd of qadhf.

Core Idea
Testimony for zina requires four legally capable witnesses; fewer or incapable witnesses turn the testimony into slander, and they receive eighty lashes.

In this lesson, we examine a ruling from the Hanafi school regarding witnesses in zina cases. The passage addresses two critical issues: the legal capacity required for witnesses and the minimum number of four. When witnesses fail either condition, their testimony is nullified, and they are punished for false accusation. The proof is from the Quran, which commands flogging those who accuse chaste women without producing four witnesses. The commentary also clarifies an objection about rejecting testimony of ascendants.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is testifying to zina. The ruling: if witnesses lack legal capacity or are fewer than four, they become liable to the hadd of qadhf (eighty lashes).
The ruling is derived from the Quranic command.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is Surah an-Nur, verse 4, which commands flogging those who accuse chaste women without bringing four witnesses.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's imperative 'flog them' applies to all who accuse chaste women without four valid witnesses. The Hanafi school includes those whose testimony is invalid due to incapacity or insufficient number.
The verse does not explicitly mention capacity, but the Hanafi interprets 'four witnesses' to mean legally capable ones.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds that a fasiq (sinner) witness is also rejected but is not automatically punished with hadd unless proven intentional lying.
This difference stems from the definition of ahliyyah (capacity).
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi school distinguishes absolute incapacity (blind, slave, non-Muslim, etc.) from moral deficiency (fasiq). Only absolute incapacity triggers the hadd of qadhf.
The fasiq still has potential capacity (ahliyyat al-tahammul wa al-ada').

Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding witnesses for zina. It addresses an objection concerning the rejection of testimony of ascendants (parents/grandparents) when descendants (children/grandchildren) testify. The commentator explains that the rejection of descendants' testimony is due to suspicion (shubha) arising from common talk, which does not apply to ascendants. He then discusses the main ruling: if witnesses lack legal capacity (e.g., blind, previously punished for qadhf, slaves, insane, etc.) or if there are fewer than four witnesses, the accused is not punished for zina; instead, the witnesses themselves are punished for qadhf (false accusation). The proof is from the Quran, Surah an-Nur, verse 4, which prescribes eighty lashes for those who accuse chaste women without bringing four witnesses. The commentator also clarifies that if some witnesses are incapable, the remaining capable ones cannot establish zina due to insufficient number, so each witness's statement becomes qadhf individually. A distinction is made between a fasiq (sinner) and those lacking capacity entirely: the fasiq still has potential capacity (ahliyyah) for testimony, but with deficiency in performance, so he is not immediately punished as a qadhif. The definition of 'muhsanat' is given as chaste, unaware women. This lesson follows the Hanafi school's position that the hadd of qadhf applies to witnesses whose testimony fails due to lack of capacity or number.

Key Terms
محدود في قذف (mahdūd fī qadhf): A person who has been punished with the hadd of eighty lashes for accusing someone of zina without proof.
أعمى (a'mā): A blind person; lacking visual perception, thus disqualified from testifying in hudud cases like zina.
نصاب (niṣāb): The required number of witnesses (four) for proving zina.
محصنات (muḥṣanāt): Chaste, free, adult Muslim women who are unaware of immoral acts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if four witnesses testify against a man for zina, but one of them is later found to be a slave?
A) The accused is still punished for zina because three valid witnesses remain.
B) The slave is punished for false accusation, but the other three are released.
C) All four are punished with the hadd of qadhf because the testimony of the slave invalidates the entire case.
D) No one is punished because the accused is innocent until proven.

Key Takeaway
In zina cases, testimony must meet both capacity and number requirements; failure turns the accusers into slanderers carrying the hadd of qadhf.

Ineligible Witnesses in Zina: All Become Liable to Hadd al-Qadhf
Ruling and proof on ineligible witnesses in zina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid zina testimony and apply the rule that if any witness is ineligible or if the required number is not met, all witnesses are liable to hadd al-qadhf.

Core Idea
Testimony for zina requires four eligible witnesses; if any is unfit, all become liable to hadd al-qadhf.

This lesson examines the first part of the passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah which deals with the consequences when witnesses in a zina case are found to be ineligible. The Hanafi school applies the Quranic verse on qadhf to punish the false witnesses themselves, establishing a clear link between the deficiency of testimony and the liability to hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for valid zina testimony
The text requires four eligible witnesses: free, adult, Muslim, upright (adl), not blind, not previously flogged for qadhf. If any is missing, the testimony fails.
Eligibility is stricter here than for other criminal cases because zina proofs are uniquely demanding.
2
Classify the defects mentioned
Defects include: being a mahdud fi qadhf, having only three witnesses, one being a slave, or discovery after hadd of such a defect.
Each defect makes the entire testimony invalid, not just the individual witness.
3
Apply the Quranic proof
The verse An-Nur 24:4 commands flogging those who accuse chaste women without four witnesses. Hanafi usul interprets the imperative 'fajliduhum' as wujub. When testimony fails, each witness's statement becomes an independent qadhf.
The proof is dalalah qati'ah (definitive meaning) per Hanafi usul.
4
Distinguish from fasiq witnesses
A fasiq still has inherent eligibility (ahl) but a deficiency in delivery, so they are not flogged. In contrast, the blind or mahdud have no eligibility at all.
This distinction prevents blanket liability for all defective testimonies.
5
Derive the ruling
All witnesses in the defective set are flogged for qadhf (80 lashes each) because the testimony as a whole is insufficient to prove zina.
The ruling applies even if the accused was guilty in reality.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
