Book of Hudud, Chapter on Testimony of Zina and Retraction therefrom.

'Or [if the witnesses are] those who have been punished for qadhf, or three, or one of them is a hadd-punished person (for qadhf), or a slave, or it is found that they are such after the hadd [has been inflicted], they are to be flogged' - due to lack of eligibility for testimony, or lack of the required number, so the hadd becomes obligatory due to His saying, the Exalted: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses - flog them eighty lashes' (Surah An-Nur 4) the verse.
If you say: When eligibility is lacking in some, the hadd should only be enforced against that one. I say: Since some witnesses were not eligible, the testimony of the remaining ones with eligibility does not prove zina due to lack of the required number, so the statement of each becomes qadhf, thus each is flogged.
[1] His saying: 'or those punished in qadhf' - meaning they had accused someone and were flogged a hadd for qadhf, and it will come that the person flogged for qadhf never has his testimony accepted, even if he repents and does righteous deeds. [2] His saying: 'or three' - meaning the witnesses were three. [3] His saying: 'or it is found... etc.' - meaning four testified against a man for zina, so he was flogged on their testimony, then one of them was found to be a slave or a hadd-punished person for qadhf or a minor or the like - the hadd is established against them because they are qadhf-makers due to incompleteness of the required number of witnesses. [4] His saying: 'due to lack of eligibility for testimony' - this is in the case of them being blind or hadd-punished for qadhf and the like. If you say: It has passed that if the witnesses were corrupt (fasiq) they would not be flogged, even though the fasiq is also not eligible for testimony. I say: It has passed that eligibility in the fasiq is not absolutely nonexistent, for the fasiq is inherently eligible to receive and deliver testimony, but in his delivery there is a kind of deficiency, unlike our case. [5] His saying: 'or lack of the required number' - this is in the case of the witnesses being three, and in the case of one of them being ineligible for testimony, and in the case of some of them appearing ineligible after the hadd. [6] His saying: 'the chaste women' (al-muhsanat) - with a fatha over the sad - meaning pure women who are heedless of lewd acts.

'And the compensation (arsh) for the wound of his flogging is null, and the blood-money (diya) for his stoning is from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) and arsh' (171). Wound (2) of his flogging is null, and the blood-money for his stoning is from the public treasury' - meaning: the witnesses testified for zina, and the adulterer was not muhsan (i.e., unmarried) so he was flogged, and the flogging wounded him, then one of the witnesses appeared to be a slave or a hadd-punished person for qadhf - then the arsh of the flogging is null according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: from the public treasury; because the act of the flogger is transferred to the judge, and he is a worker for the Muslims, so the liability is from the wealth of the Muslims. And for him (Abu Hanifa): The wounding act is not transferred to the judge because he did not order the wound, so it is confined to the flogger. Then it is... [1] His saying: 'and arsh' - with a fatha on the hamza: the blood-money, and 'hadr' - with a fatha - meaning null, in Persian 'raykan', and likewise if the flogged person dies from the beating, then the blood-money for the person is obligatory from the public treasury according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) if some witnesses appear to be a slave or hadd-punished for qadhf or blind, and according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, nothing is obligatory. This is mentioned in al-'Inayah (3). [2] His saying: 'because... etc.' - its summary: The wound only occurred due to the flogging, and although it is the act of the flogger, it is transferred to the judge because he flogged him by the judge's order, and the judge is a worker for the Muslims, so the liability resulting from his action is from the wealth of the Muslims, and its place is the public treasury. [3] His saying: 'the wounding act' - with the description meaning the act that wounded him, and in some copies: 'act of the wounder' in construct, so the intended by 'the wounder' is the flogger, and by his act he wounded him. [4] His saying: 'because he did not order the wound' - its summary: The obligatory [act] is flogging, which is a painful beating that does not cause a wound nor is fatal, and the judge's order only pertains to what is obligatory, and flogging only becomes wounding due to something in the beater, namely lack of care, so that act is confined to the flogger and is not transferred to the judge so that liability would be from the public treasury. [5] His saying: 'then it is... etc.' - a rebuttal of an anticipated objection. The objection's statement: Since the wounding act is confined to the flogger, it becomes obligatory that the flogger should be liable, even if liability is not on the judge or the public treasury.
Source pages p. 215

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Hudud (Hadd penalties) in the chapter on testimony for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) and retraction deals with two main rulings: (1) When witnesses in a zina case are found to be ineligible after the hadd penalty has been carried out, they themselves are to be punished for qadhf (false accusation). (2) The compensation (arsh or diya) for injuries or death resulting from the flogging or stoning that was based on their testimony.

The passage begins by stating that if some witnesses are ineligible—for example, they have previously been flogged for qadhf (which permanently disqualifies them from testifying), or there are only three witnesses instead of four, or one is a slave, or it is discovered after the hadd has been inflicted that a witness is a slave or a person punished for qadhf—then all the witnesses are to be flogged for qadhf. The reason is that their testimony is invalid either because of lack of eligibility (like blindness, having been punished for qadhf, etc.) or because the required number of witnesses (four) was not met. The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah An-Nur (24:4), which commands flogging those who accuse chaste women without producing four witnesses.

The text addresses a potential objection: if only some witnesses are ineligible, why are all flogged? The answer is that since the full set of four eligible witnesses is not present, the testimony does not establish zina, so the statement of each witness becomes a false accusation (qadhf), and each is liable to the hadd for qadhf.

A distinction is made between a fasiq (sinner who is not upright) and those who are categorically ineligible (like the blind or those flogged for qadhf). A fasiq still has some inherent eligibility for testimony (they can receive and deliver testimony), but their delivery may have deficiency. In contrast, those permanently disqualified have no eligibility at all.

The second part discusses compensation (arsh for wounds, diya for death) when it is discovered after the flogging (for an unmarried offender) or after stoning (for a married offender) that a witness was ineligible. According to Abu Hanifa, the compensation for the flogging wound is null (hadr) because the wounding act is attributed to the flogger, not the judge, since the judge only ordered flogging (which is not supposed to cause injury). The flogger acted carelessly, so he alone is liable if anything. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the compensation is from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) because the flogger acted under the judge's order, and the judge is a public official, so liability falls on the Muslim treasury. If the flogged person dies, the same dispute applies: the two disciples say diya is from bayt al-mal, Abu Hanifa says nothing is due because the execution of a valid legal punishment (hadd) is not wrongful, and the injury or death is attributed to the flogger's negligence.

The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the key terms: 'arsh' is blood-money for wounds, 'hadr' means null or invalid. The text also clarifies that the judge's order is limited to a non-wounding, non-lethal flogging, so any harm beyond that is the flogger's responsibility.

Key Terms
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed penalty for false accusation of zina: eighty lashes.
محدود في قذف (mahdud fi qadhf): A person who has been flogged for qadhf; such a person is permanently disqualified from testifying.
أهلية الشهادة (ahliyyat al-shahada): Eligibility to testify; in zina cases, requires the witness to be free, adult, Muslim, upright, and not blind or previously flogged for qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Four witnesses testify against a man for zina. One is blind. After the accused is flogged, it is discovered that a blind man's testimony is invalid. What happens to the witnesses?
A) Only the blind man is flogged for qadhf.
B) All four are flogged for qadhf.
C) None are flogged because the accused was guilty.
D) They are only reprimanded.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, any deficiency in the eligibility or number of witnesses in a zina case renders all witnesses liable to hadd al-qadhf.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Compensation for Flogging or Stoning Based on Invalid Testimony: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on compensation for judicial error in hudud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding arsh/diya for injuries or death from hadd punishments executed on invalid testimony, and identify the practical consequences.

Core Idea
When witnesses are later found ineligible, liability for harm from the hadd punishment is disputed: Abu Hanifa says it's null (hadr); the Sahibayn say it's from bayt al-mal.

This lesson focuses on the second part of the passage, which addresses the compensation for wounds or death resulting from flogging or stoning when it is discovered that the witnesses were ineligible. The Hanafi school is divided on who bears the financial liability, with implications for the public treasury.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Witnesses testify, the zina punishment (flogging for non-muhsan, stoning for muhsan) is carried out, and then a witness is found to be ineligible (e.g., slave, mahdud fi qadhf, blind).
The discovery occurs after the punishment has been executed.
2
Note the type of harm
If flogging wounds the accused, the issue is arsh (compensation for wounds). If stoning causes death, the issue is diya (blood-money).
The text covers both types of harm.
3
State the dispute
Abu Hanifa rules that the arsh for a flogging wound is null (hadr) and no diya is due for death. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) rule that both arsh and diya are payable from the public treasury (bayt al-mal).
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf, not a dispute between madhhabs.
4
Analyze the reasoning
Abu Hanifa: The judge's order was for non-wounding flogging; any injury results from the flogger's negligence, so liability rests solely with the flogger, not transferred to the judge or state. The Sahibayn: The flogger acted under the judge's order; the judge is a public official, so his act is attributed to the treasury.
The key difference is whether the flogger's act is 'transferred' to the judge.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Under Abu Hanifa, the victim or heirs get nothing from the state. Under Sahibayn, they receive compensation from bayt al-mal.
The mufta bihi in later Hanafi practice is the Sahibayn view, ensuring victims are not left uncompensated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

أو محدودين في قذف أو ثلاثة، أو أحدهم محدود، أو عبد، أو وُجد كذلك بعد الحد حدوا)؛ لعدم أهلية الشهادة، أو عدم النصاب، فيجب الحد لقوله تعالى: وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَاتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَانِينَ جَلْدَةً (1) الآية.
فإن قلت: إذا لم تكن الأهلية في البعض يجب أن لا يقام الحدّ إلا عليه. قلت: لما لم يكن بعض الشهودِ أهلاً فشهادة الباقيين مع الأهلية غير مثبتة للزنا؛ لعدم النصاب فصار كلام كل منهما قذفاً، فيحد كل منهم.
[1] قوله: أو محدودين في قذف؛ بأن كانوا قذفوا أحداً فحدوا حداً بقذف وسيأتي أن المحدود في قذف لا تقبل له شهادة أبداً وإن تاب وعمل عملاً صالحاً. [2] قوله: أو ثلاثة؛ أي كانت الشهداء ثلاثة. [3] قوله: أو وجد... الخ؛ يعني شهد أربعة على رجل بالزنا، فضرب بشهادتهم ثم وجد أحدهم عبداً أو محدوداً في قذف أو صبياً أو نحو ذلك أقيم عليهم الحد؛ لكونهم قذفة؛ لعدم تمام نصاب الشهادة. [4] قوله: لعدم أهلية الشهادة؛ هذا في صورة كونهم عمياناً أو محدودين في قذف ونحو ذلك. فإن قلت: قد مرّ أنّ الشهود لو كانوا فسقة لم يحدّوا مع أن الفاسق أيضاً ليس بأهل للشهادة. قلت: قد مرّ أنّ الأهلية في الفاسق ليست بمفقودة مطلقاً، فإنّ الفاسق في نفسه أهل للشهادةِ تحمّلاً وأداء نعم في أدائه نوع قصور، بخلاف ما نحن فيه. [5] قوله: أو عدم النصاب؛ هذا في صورة كون الشهداء ثلاثة، وفي صورة كون أحدهم غير أهل للشهادة، وفي صورة ظهور بعضهم غير أهل بعد الحد. [6] قوله: المحصنات؛ - بفتح الصاد المهملة -؛ أي النساء العفائف الغافلات عن الفواحش.

وأرش جرح جلده هدر، ودية رجمه في بيت المال وارش (171). جرح (2) جلدِهِ هَدْر، وديةً رجمِهِ في بيت المال): أي شهدَ الشُّهُودُ بالزنا، والزاني غير محصن فجلد، فجرَحَهُ الجلد، ثُمَّ ظهر أحد الشُّهودِ عبداً، أو محدوداً في قذف فأرش الجلدِ هَدْرٌ عند أبي حنيفة له وقالا: في بيت المال؛ لأن فعل الجلادِ ينتقل إلى القاضي، وهو عامل للمسلمين، فالغرامة في مال المسلمين. وله: إنَّ الفعل الجارح لا ينتقل إلى القاضي؛ لأنه لم يأمر بالجرح، فيقتصر على الجلاد، ثُمَّ هواه [1] قوله: وأرش؛ - بفتح الهمزة -: الدية، والهــدر: – بالفتح – بمعنى الباطل، بالفارسية رايكان، وكذا إذا مات المجلود من الضرب فتجب دية النفس في بيت المال عندهما إذا ظهر بعض الشهودِ عبداً أو محدوداً في قذف أو أعمى، وعند أبي حنيفة له لا يجب شيء. كذا في «العناية»(3). [2] قوله: لأنّ... الخ؛ حاصله: إنّ الجرحَ إنما حصل بسبب الجلد، وهو وإن كان فعلُ الجلاد لكنه منتقل إلى القاضي؛ لأنه جلده بأمر القاضي، والقاضي عامل للمسلمين، فتكون الغرامة الحاصلة بفعله في مال المسلمين، وموضعه بيت المال. [3] قوله: الفعل الجارح؛ بالتوصيف أي الفعل الذي جرحه، وفي بعض النسخ: فعل الجارح بالإضافة، فالمراد بالجارح هو الجلاد، وبفعله جرحه. [4] قوله: لأنه لم يأمر بالجرح؛ حاصله: إنّ الواجب هو الجلد، وهو ضرب مؤلم غير خارج ولا مهلك، وأمرُ القاضي إنّما يتعلّق بما هو الواجب، ولا يقع الجلد جارحاً إلا لمعنى في الضارب، وهو قلة اهتمامه فيقتصر ذلك الفعل على الجلاد، ولا ينتقل إلى القاضي لتجب الغرامة في بيت المال. [5] قوله: ثم هو.... الخ؛ دفعُ دخل مقدّر، تقرير الدخل: أنه لما اقتصر الفعلُ الجارح على الجلاد وَجَبَ أن يضمن الجلاد، وإن لم يجب الضمان على القاضي أو في بيت المال.

'Or [if the witnesses are] those who have been punished for qadhf, or three, or one of them is a hadd-punished person (for qadhf), or a slave, or it is found that they are such after the hadd [has been inflicted], they are to be flogged' - due to lack of eligibility for testimony, or lack of the required number, so the hadd becomes obligatory due to His saying, the Exalted: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses - flog them eighty lashes' (Surah An-Nur 4) the verse.

Commentary
This passage from the Book of Hudud (Hadd penalties) in the chapter on testimony for zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) and retraction deals with two main rulings: (1) When witnesses in a zina case are found to be ineligible after the hadd penalty has been carried out, they themselves are to be punished for qadhf (false accusation). (2) The compensation (arsh or diya) for injuries or death resulting from the flogging or stoning that was based on their testimony.

The passage begins by stating that if some witnesses are ineligible—for example, they have previously been flogged for qadhf (which permanently disqualifies them from testifying), or there are only three witnesses instead of four, or one is a slave, or it is discovered after the hadd has been inflicted that a witness is a slave or a person punished for qadhf—then all the witnesses are to be flogged for qadhf. The reason is that their testimony is invalid either because of lack of eligibility (like blindness, having been punished for qadhf, etc.) or because the required number of witnesses (four) was not met. The proof is the Quranic verse from Surah An-Nur (24:4), which commands flogging those who accuse chaste women without producing four witnesses.

The text addresses a potential objection: if only some witnesses are ineligible, why are all flogged? The answer is that since the full set of four eligible witnesses is not present, the testimony does not establish zina, so the statement of each witness becomes a false accusation (qadhf), and each is liable to the hadd for qadhf.

A distinction is made between a fasiq (sinner who is not upright) and those who are categorically ineligible (like the blind or those flogged for qadhf). A fasiq still has some inherent eligibility for testimony (they can receive and deliver testimony), but their delivery may have deficiency. In contrast, those permanently disqualified have no eligibility at all.

The second part discusses compensation (arsh for wounds, diya for death) when it is discovered after the flogging (for an unmarried offender) or after stoning (for a married offender) that a witness was ineligible. According to Abu Hanifa, the compensation for the flogging wound is null (hadr) because the wounding act is attributed to the flogger, not the judge, since the judge only ordered flogging (which is not supposed to cause injury). The flogger acted carelessly, so he alone is liable if anything. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the compensation is from the public treasury (bayt al-mal) because the flogger acted under the judge's order, and the judge is a public official, so liability falls on the Muslim treasury. If the flogged person dies, the same dispute applies: the two disciples say diya is from bayt al-mal, Abu Hanifa says nothing is due because the execution of a valid legal punishment (hadd) is not wrongful, and the injury or death is attributed to the flogger's negligence.

The commentary from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah explains the key terms: 'arsh' is blood-money for wounds, 'hadr' means null or invalid. The text also clarifies that the judge's order is limited to a non-wounding, non-lethal flogging, so any harm beyond that is the flogger's responsibility.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Compensation for wounds; measured as a fraction of full diya.
هدر (hadr): Null, void; no compensation due.
بيت المال (bayt al-mal): Public treasury of the Islamic state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on arsh for a flogging wound when a witness is later found to be ineligible?
A) Arsh is always null (hadr) according to all Hanafi imams.
B) Arsh is from bayt al-mal according to Abu Hanifa and null according to the Sahibayn.
C) Arsh is null according to Abu Hanifa and from bayt al-mal according to the Sahibayn.
D) Arsh is payable by the flogger in all cases.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a legitimate ikhtilaf on whether the state compensates for harm from judicial errors in hadd cases; the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that compensation comes from bayt al-mal.

Hudud — Fixed Penalties

Liability and Retraction in Hudud Cases
Explaining liability for injuries from hadd executions and the hadd for a retracting witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on liability for injuries from hadd punishments and explain the ruling on a retracting witness after rajm.

Core Idea
A witness who retracts after stoning is subject to hadd qadhf, but compensation for unintended injuries from the execution is generally from the public treasury.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'aya addresses the legal consequences when witnesses in a zina case are later found to be defective or retract their testimony. It involves three key scenarios: injury from lashing (jald), death from stoning (rajm), and retraction after stoning. The rulings differ between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), with a further difference from Zufar on the retraction issue. Understanding these disputes clarifies how the Hanafi school balances protecting individuals' rights with ensuring that hudud penalties are not nullified.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three scenarios
The passage discusses: (1) a non-muhsan is lashed and wounded, (2) a muhsan is stoned and dies, (3) one of the four witnesses retracts after stoning. Note the legal issue in each.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
For jald wounds, Abu Hanifa says arsh is hader (no compensation). For rajm death, he agrees diyah is in bayt al-mal. For retraction, he holds the witness is subject to hadd qadhf.
3
State Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say arsh for jald wounds is paid from bayt al-mal, and if the person dies, diyah is also from bayt al-mal. On retraction, they agree with Abu Hanifa that hadd qadhf applies.
4
Explain the reasoning for the dispute
Abu Hanifa argues that the wounding act does not transfer to the judge because the judge only ordered non-wounding lashing; the lashinger's own negligence caused the wound, but to avoid discouraging hadd, no liability falls on the lashinger either. Sahibayn argue that the act transfers to the judge as an agent for Muslims, so the public treasury bears the cost.
5
Analyze the retraction dispute with Zufar
Zufar argued that the retracting witness should not be lashed because the accusation would be either before or after rajm, both problematic. The majority responds that the retraction turns the testimony into qadhf at the moment of retraction, and the doubt created by the judge's ruling does not prevent the hadd.
The practical difference: under the majority, the retractor is lashed; under Zufar, he is not.

And the compensation for the wound of his lashing is wasted, and the blood money for his stoning is in the public treasury. (171) Wound (2) of his skin is wasted, and the blood money for his stoning in the public treasury. That is: The witnesses testified to zina, and the fornicator is not muhsan so he was lashed, and the lashing wounded him, then one of the witnesses appeared to be a slave or one who had been lashed for qadhf, so the compensation for the lashing is wasted according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: in the public treasury, because the act of the lashinger transfers to the judge, and he is an agent for the Muslims, so the liability is in the wealth of the Muslims. And for him (Abu Hanifa): Indeed, the wounding act does not transfer to the judge, because he did not order the wound, so it is confined to the lashinger. Then he said... (etc.) ... And if they testified and the fornicator is muhsan and he was stoned, then one of them appeared to be a slave or the like, then the blood money of the stoning is in the public treasury. (2) His saying: in the public treasury; this is agreed upon, and its explanation is that the stoning is attributed to their testimony, so they guarantee by retraction, and when there is no retraction it is obligatory in the public treasury because his stoning is attributed to the order of the judge, and he is an agent for the Muslims, so the liability is in their wealth, unlike lashing, because what was ordered there is non-wounding lashing, so the wounding act does not transfer to the judge, but is confined to the lashinger. And if one of the four retracts after stoning, he is subject to a hadd (punishment) and does not guarantee, so that people are not prevented from carrying out (the hadd) for fear of liability. (And if one of the four retracts after stoning, he is subject to a hadd): meaning the hadd of the retractor is only the hadd of qadhf, and according to Zufar, he is not subject to hadd. The gist of the argument and response: Zufar said: The hadd is not obligatory on the retractor; because if it were obligatory, it would either be for qadhf before the stoning – but that is not possible because if someone accuses a living person of zina and then the accused dies, the accuser is not lashed since it is not inherited – or for qadhf after the stoning – also not possible because the stoned person is not accused due to the judge's ruling, which creates a doubt, making it like someone else accusing him. Our argument: His words are not qadhf at the moment; rather, they constituted a testimony and ruling occurred based on that description, but upon retraction it turns into qadhf because he rescinds his testimony after its existence, so what is built upon it (the judgment) is nullified, making it qadhf at the moment, and it is pure (qadhf) in his claim, so he is lashed, unlike if someone else accused him; also because the stoned person was stoned by the judge's ruling and no rescission of testimony occurred regarding him, since the retractor's claim applies to himself, not to others. See al-Tabyin 3:192.
Source pages p. 216

Commentary
This passage covers several rulings related to the consequences when witnesses in a zina case are later found to be defective or retract. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute and a commentary expanding on the matn of al-Wiqaya. First, the matn states that if a non-muhsan fornicator is lashed and wounded, the arsh (compensation for the wound) is wasted (hader) according to Abu Hanifa, but the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say it is paid from the public treasury. The disagreement hinges on whether the act of the lashinger transfers to the judge: Abu Hanifa says the judge only ordered non-wounding lashing, so the wound is the lashinger's own doing and does not transfer, but then to avoid discouraging hadd execution, no liability is imposed on the lashinger either. The disciples argue that the act transfers to the judge as an agent of the Muslims, so the public treasury pays. If the lashinge dies, the disciples impose diyah in the public treasury, while Abu Hanifa says nothing. For the case of a muhsan who is stoned and then a witness is found defective, there is agreement that the diyah is in the public treasury because the stoning is attributed to the witnesses' testimony, but if they do not retract, it goes back to the judge's order. The passage then addresses a witness who retracts after stoning: he is not liable for diyah (to avoid deterring enforcement), but he is subject to the hadd of qadhf (false accusation). Zufar ibn al-Hudhayl disagreed, arguing that the retractor should not be lashed because the accusation is either before or after stoning, both of which create doubts. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) respond that his testimony, once retracted, retroactively becomes qadhf, so he is lashed.

Key Terms
أرش (arsh): Compensation for a wound or injury less than death; akin to diyah for wounds.
هدَر (hader): Wasted, null; no compensation is due.
دية (diyah): Blood money for homicide or loss of life.
رجع (raja'a): To retract one's testimony.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for false accusation of zina, which is 80 lashes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on a witness who retracts after the accused has been stoned to death?
A) He is not liable for anything because the execution is final.
B) He must pay diyah from his own wealth.
C) He is subject to the hadd of qadhf (80 lashes).
D) He is imprisoned for life.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a witness who retracts after rajm is liable for hadd qadhf, but compensation for unintended injuries from jald or rajm is generally from the public treasury to avoid discouraging hadd enforcement.

Witness Retraction After Stoning: The Hadd of Qadhf
Intra-Hanafi dispute on hadd qadhf after retraction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a witness who retracts after rajm, explain Zufar's objection, and apply the Hanafi response based on annulment of the judge's order.

Core Idea
Retraction annuls the testimony from its root; no doubt remains to prevent hadd qadhf.

The integrity of hudud punishments relies on the unwavering testimony of witnesses. When a witness retracts after the accused has been executed, the law must balance the finality of the punishment with the rights of the accused and the accuser. This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether a retracting witness faces the hadd of false accusation (qadhf) or is protected by doubt (shubha). The ruling has practical implications for the administration of justice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and the disputed point
The general rule: if one of four witnesses retracts after stoning, he incurs the hadd of qadhf. The dispute is whether this hadd is actually applicable. Zufar argues it is not, while the three imams say it is.
The other three witnesses are not liable because they did not retract.
2
Understand Zufar's two-part objection
Zufar considers two possibilities: (1) if the retraction is seen as an accusation during the accused's life, the hadd of qadhf falls by death; (2) if after death, the accused died by a judge's order based on testimony, which creates a doubt (shubha) that prevents the hadd.
The principle: hadd is dropped by doubt.
3
Analyze the majority Hanafi response
The three imams choose the second possibility (accusation after death) but argue that the judge's order was contingent on the testimony. Since the retraction annuls the testimony, the order is annulled from its root, so the accused was never legally stoned. Thus no doubt remains.
This response preserves the hadd for the retractor.
4
Determine the operative ruling (mufta bihi)
The majority view is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) per al-Hidayah and works of later Hanafi scholars. The retractor is subject to hadd qadhf.
This is from the Zahir al-Riwayah, the core Hanafi texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأي رَجَعَ من الأربعةِ بعد رَجم حدّ لا يضمن ؛ لئلا يمتنع النَّاسُ عن الإقامة مخافة للغرامة. وإن شهدوا والزَّانِي محصنٌ فَرحِم ، ثُمَّ ظَهَرَ أَحدُهم عبداً أو نحوه فديَةُ الرَّحِمِ في بيت المال". (واي" رَجَعَ من الأربعة بعد رجم حدٌ) : أي حد الراجع فقط حد القذف وعند زفر له لا يحد. وحاصل الدفع : إنّ الضمان لا يجب على الجلاد مطلقاً، كيلا يمتنع الناس عن إقامة هذا الحدّ لخوف وجوب الغرامة عليهم. (١) قوله : لا يضمن ؛ هذا هو الصحيح كما في «الهداية ، قال في «العناية»: يعني في الصحيح من الرواية، وذكر في مبسوط فخرِ الإسلام»: لو قال قائل : يجب الضمان على الجلاد ، فله وجه ؛ لأنه ليس بمأمور بهذا الوجه ؛ لأنه أمر بضرب مؤلم لا جارح ولا كاسر ولا قاتل ، فإذا وجد منه الضرب على هذه الوجوه وقع فعله تعديا ، فيجب عليه الضمان. (٢) قوله : في بيت المال ؛ هذا اتفاقي، ووجهه أنّ الرجم مضاف إلى شهادتهم ، فيضمنون بالرجوع، وعند عدم الرجوع يجب في بيت المال ؛ لأن رجمه مضاف إلى أمر القاضي، وهو عامل للمسلمين، فتجب الغرامة في مالهم ، بخلاف الجلد، فإنّ المأمور به هناك هو الجلد الغير الجارح ، فالفعلُ الجارح لا ينتقل إلى القاضي ، بل يقتصر على الجلاد. [٣]قوله : وأي ؛ - بفتح الهمزة وتشديد الياء - : أي أي الشهود الأربعة رجع عن شهادته بعدما رجم المشهود عليه فقال : كذبتُ في شهادتي، أقيم على ذلك الراجع حد القذف فقط ؛ لأنه صار قاذفاً، ولا حدّ على الباقين لعدم صدور القذف عنهم؛ لبقائهم على شهادتهم. [ ١ ] قوله : لأنه ... الخ ؛ حاصله : إنّ الراجع وإن صار قاذفاً برجوعه لكن لا يخلو إما أن يكون قاذفاً فالمرجوم في حياته قبل رجمه بناءً على أنّ بالرجوع أخبر أنه كذب في شهادة نسبته إلى الزنا، وكان ذلك في حياته، فيكون قاذفا عند ذلك. وإما أن يكون قاذفاً للمرجوم بعد مماته بالرجم ، بناءً على أن القذف ثبت بالرجوع وهو بعد موته. وعلى كل تقدير : فلا وجه لإقامة حد القذف على الراجع، أما على الأول فلأنّ حد القذف يسقط بموت المقذوف، ولا يورث عنه على ما تقرر في موضعه، وأما على الثاني فلأنّ المقذوف مرجومٌ بحكم القاضي بزناه، وهو إن لم يسقط الإحصان فلا أقل من أن يورث شبهة، والحد يبطل بالشبهة. [٢] قوله : فلا يجب الحد ؛ هكذا في بعض النسخ ، وفي بعضها بدله : ويورث ذلك شبهة فلا يجب الحد لعدم الإحصان. انتهى. [٣]قوله : قلنا... الخ ؛ جواب عن دليل زفر له من قبل أئمتنا الثلاثة، وحاصله : إنا نختار الشق الثاني، وهو أن الراجع قاذف مرجوم بعد موته، وكونه مرجوماً بحكم القاضي كان موقوفاً على الشهادة ، وإذ قد بطلت برجوع الشاهد انفسح حكم القاضي من أصله، فلم يبق المرجوم مرجوماً بحكم القاضي، فلم يبطل الإحصان ولم تعرض شبهة تسقط الحد.
And whoever among the four [witnesses] retracts after stoning incurs a hadd—he is not liable [for damages] so that people do not refrain from carrying out [the hadd] for fear of liability. If they testified and the adulterer was muhsan and was stoned, then one of them turned out to be a slave or the like, the blood money for the stoning is from the public treasury. "And whoever among the four retracts after stoning incurs a hadd": meaning the hadd of the retractor only is the hadd of qadhf, and according to Zufar he does not incur the hadd. The summary of the response: Liability is not obligated on the executioner absolutely, so that people do not refrain from carrying out this hadd for fear of liability upon them. (1) His statement: "he is not liable"; this is the correct [view] as in al-Hidayah. He said in al-Inayah: meaning in the correct narration. And it is mentioned in Mabsut of Fakhr al-Islam: if someone said, liability is obligated on the executioner, he has a basis because he was not commanded to do so in this manner; he was commanded to inflict painful beating, not wounding, breaking, or killing. If he inflicts beating in these ways, his action becomes transgression, so liability is obligated on him. (2) His statement: "from the public treasury"; this is agreed upon. Its reasoning is that the stoning is attributed to their testimony, so they are liable upon retraction. When there is no retraction, it is obligated from the public treasury because the stoning is attributed to the judge's order, and he is an agent for the Muslims, so the blood money is obligated from their wealth, unlike lashing, because the commanded act there is lashing that does not wound, so the wounding act is not transferred to the judge but is restricted to the executioner. [3] His statement: "And whoever"—with fatha on the hamza and tashdid on the ya—meaning whichever of the four witnesses retracts his testimony after the accused was stoned and says, "I lied in my testimony," that retractor is subjected only to the hadd of qadhf because he became an accuser, and there is no hadd on the others because no accusation issued from them; due to their remaining on their testimony. [1] His statement: "because..." etc.; its summary: the retractor, although he becomes an accuser by his retraction, is not free from either being an accuser of the stoned person during his life before stoning, based on the idea that by retraction he informs that he lied in the testimony attributing zina to him, and that was during his life, so he becomes an accuser at that time, or being an accuser of the stoned person after his death by stoning, based on the idea that the accusation is established by retraction and it is after his death. In either case, there is no basis for establishing the hadd of qadhf on the retractor. As for the first, because the hadd of qadhf falls by the death of the accused and is not inherited from him as established in its place. As for the second, because the accused was stoned by the judge's order due to his zina, and if this does not remove ihsan, at least it creates a doubt, and the hadd is invalidated by doubt. [2] His statement: "so the hadd is not obligated"; thus in some copies, and in others instead: "and that creates a doubt, so the hadd is not obligated due to lack of ihsan." End. [3] His statement: "We say..." etc.; a response to Zufar's evidence from the three imams. Its summary: We choose the second possibility, which is that the retractor is an accuser of the stoned person after his death. And his being stoned by the judge's order depended on the testimony, and since it is invalidated by the witness's retraction, the judge's order is annulled from its root. Thus the stoned person is no longer stoned by the judge's order, so ihsan is not removed and no doubt arises to drop the hadd.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on a witness who retracts his testimony after the accused has been stoned to death for zina. The passage type is an intra-Hanafi dispute, specifically the opinion of Imam Zufar against the majority (the three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The text begins by stating a general principle: if one of the four witnesses retracts after stoning, he incurs the hadd of qadhf (false accusation). However, according to Zufar, he does not incur the hadd. The reasoning of the majority is that the retraction transforms his testimony into an accusation of zina against a dead person. Zufar argues that if the accusation is considered during the life of the accused, the hadd falls by death; if after death, the accused was stoned by the judge's order, creating a doubt that prevents the hadd. The Hanafi response (from the three imams) is that they choose the second possibility (accusation after death), but they argue that the judge's order was based on the testimony, and since the retraction annuls the testimony, the order is annulled from its root, so no doubt remains to drop the hadd. Thus, the retractor is subject to the hadd of qadhf. The other three witnesses are not liable because they maintained their testimony. This ruling is from the Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position.

Key Terms
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed punishment for false accusation of zina, which is eighty lashes.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as the punishment for muhsan adulterers.
شبهة (shubhah): A legal doubt that prevents the application of a hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab (majority opinion), what is the ruling on a witness who retracts his testimony after the accused has been stoned for zina?
A) He is subject to the hadd of qadhf.
B) He is not subject to any punishment because the accused died.
C) He is subject to the same punishment as the accused (stoning).
D) He must pay blood money to the accused's family.

Key Takeaway
The retraction of a witness after rajm annuls the judge's order from its root, eliminating any doubt, so the retractor incurs the hadd of qadhf.

8 min
Ruling on a Witness Who Retracts After Stoning
Explains Hanafi ruling on retracting witness after stoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for a witness who retracts after the accused is stoned, explain the qiyas reasoning that supports it, and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A retracting witness in a zina case becomes a slanderer and must pay diya, not face retaliation, because stoning is analogous to killing and Hanafis prefer compensation.

This lesson examines a specific scenario in hudud: what happens when a witness in a zina case retracts after the accused has already been stoned. The Hanafi school addresses this through a careful analysis of the legal effects of retraction, considering both the hadd for slander (qadhf) and financial compensation (diya). We will explore the reasoning of the three imams against Zufar's objection, and compare with al-Shafi'i's approach.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? A witness retracts testimony after the accused has been stoned for zina. According to the Hanafi school, the witness is subject to two consequences: hadd qadhf and payment of a quarter of the diya.
The ruling applies to each retracting witness individually.
2
Understand the intra-madhhab dispute
Zufar argued that no hadd is required because either the slandered is dead (hadd falls) or he is stoned by judge's ruling (creates doubt). The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) respond that the retraction annuls the judge's ruling, removing the doubt, so the witness becomes a slanderer and must receive hadd.
This dispute is resolved in favor of the three imams.
3
Trace the Hanafi dalil: qiyas
The Hanafi school analogizes this case to witnesses in homicide who retract after execution. In both cases, the false testimony leads to death. Hanafis require diya (blood-money) rather than qisas (retaliation) for such witnesses; here, the same principle applies, with stoning being equivalent to killing.
Shafi'is disagree, applying qisas for false witnesses in murder cases.
4
Note the inter-madhhab dispute
Al-Shafi'i holds that the retracting witness must face retaliation (qisas) by the heirs of the executed person. The Hanafi school responds that their principle is to impose diya, not qisas, on false witnesses in capital cases.
The thamar al-khilaf: Hanafi witness pays diya; Shafi'i witness could be killed.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the retracting witness receives hadd qadhf and pays a quarter of the diya. This is based on the majority of the early Hanafi masters and is the operative ruling for fatwa.
This position is from the zahir al-riwayah.

وغَرِمَ رُبعَ الدّية : هذا عندنا ، وعند الشافعي (١) له يقتص بناءً على أصله في شهودِ القصاص، كما قال في الديات"
وقبله حدُّوا فقط) : أي رجع من الأربعة حد جميعُ الشُّهودِ حد القذف، ولا يحد المشهود عليه
[1] قوله : وغرم ؛ أي وجب على الراجع أن يضمن ربع دية النفس، فإن رجعوا كلهم وجبت عليهم الدية كاملة.
[٢] قوله : بناءً على أصله... الخ ؛ فإنّ شهود القتل عمداً الموجب للقصاص إذا رجعوا بعدما قتل المشهود عليه ، فعند الشافعي يجب عليهم القصاص، وعندنا الدية، فكذا هاهنا فإنّ الرجم في حكم القتل .
[٣]قوله : كما قال في الديات ؛ ظاهره أنّ هذه المسألة ذكرها المصنف ه في بحث الديات، وهو حوالة غير صحيحة، فإنّه لا أثر لهذه المسألة لا في المتن ولا في الشرح في «كتاب الديات»، نعم لها ذكر في «كتاب الشهادة» في «فصل منعقد لذكر مسائل الرجوع عنها، حيث قال المصنف له هناك : «وفي القصاص الدية فقط»، وقال الشارح : «أي إذا شهدا أنّ زيداً قتل عمراً فاقتص زيد، ثم رجعـا تجـب الـديـة عندنا ، ، وعند الشافعي له يقتص». انتهى.
وقد وقع الخطأ في هذا المقام عن صاحب الهداية» في الحوالة إلى «كتاب الديات» أيضاً، فطالعها إن شئت. ولنا : توجيه يحفظ به كلام الشارح . هاهنا الخطأ، وهو أن يقال : ضمير قال عن راجع إلى الشافعي له لا إلى المصنّف ، ويكون المقصود أنّ الشافعي ذكر أصله المذكور في بحث الديات.
Because if he is slandering a living person, then (the hadd) has fallen due to death; and if he is slandering a dead person, he is one stoned by the judge's ruling, so the hadd is not obligatory. We say: He is slandering a dead person; because his testimony by retraction turned into slander, so he became a slanderer after death, and the stoned person is no longer stoned by the judge's ruling, because the ruling is voided with the voiding of the evidence. When after the stoning of the convicted person he said: 'I lied in my testimony', only that retracting witness is subjected to the hadd of slander; because he became a slanderer, and there is no hadd on the others because they remained on their testimony. [1] The summary: the retractor, although he becomes a slanderer by his retraction, is either a slanderer of the stoned person during his life before stoning, based on that by retraction he informed that he lied in his testimony attributing him to zina, and that was during his life, so he is a slanderer at that time; or he is a slanderer of the stoned person after his death by stoning, based on that the slander is established by retraction and it is after his death. In either case, there is no basis for establishing the hadd of slander on the retractor. As for the first, because the hadd of slander falls with the death of the slandered, and is not inherited, as established in its place. As for the second, because the slandered is stoned by the judge's ruling due to his zina, and even if it does not nullify ihsan, it at least creates a doubt, and the hadd is nullified by doubt. [2] 'So the hadd is not obligatory' – this is in some copies, and in others it is replaced by 'and that creates a doubt so the hadd is not obligatory due to lack of ihsan.' End. [3] 'We say' – this is a response to Zufar's evidence from our three imams; its summary: we choose the second branch, which is that the retractor is a slanderer of a stoned person after his death, and his being stoned by the judge's ruling was dependent on the testimony, and since the testimony became void by the witness's retraction, the judge's ruling is annulled from its root, so the stoned person is no longer stoned by the judge's ruling, so ihsan is not nullified and no doubt occurs to nullify the hadd. (1) Because the hadd of slander is not inherited; because the predominant in it is the right of Allah, so it creates doubt. See: Al-Fath (0: ABA). (2) And that, if it does not nullify ihsan, at least creates doubt, and the hadd is nullified by doubt. See: Al-Inayah (5:293). And he pays a quarter of the blood-money, and before that they are only subject to hadd. [2] 219. 'And he pays a quarter of the blood-money' – this is with us, and with al-Shafi'i he is subject to retaliation, based on his principle in witnesses of retaliation, as he said in the book of blood-money. 'And before that they are only subject to hadd' – meaning if one of the four retracts, all witnesses are subjected to the hadd of slander, and the accused is not subjected to hadd. [1] 'And pays' – meaning it is obligatory on the retractor to guarantee a quarter of the blood-money of a life; if all retract, the full blood-money is obligatory on them. [2] 'Based on his principle' – because witnesses of intentional killing that necessitate retaliation, if they retract after the convicted is killed, according to al-Shafi'i retaliation is obligatory on them, while with us it is the blood-money; likewise here, because stoning is in the ruling of killing. [3] 'As he said in the book of blood-money' – apparently the author mentioned this issue in the discussion of blood-money, but that reference is incorrect; there is no trace of this issue in the text or commentary in the book of blood-money. Rather, it is mentioned in the book of testimony in a chapter dedicated to issues of retraction, where the author said: 'In retaliation, only the blood-money,' and the commentator said: 'If two witnesses testified that Zayd killed Amr, and Zayd was executed by retaliation, then they retracted, they owe the blood-money according to us, while according to al-Shafi'i they are subject to retaliation.' End. Indeed, an error occurred here from the author of Al-Hidayah in referring to the book of blood-money as well; so consult if you wish. And we have a justification that maintains the commentator's speech here from error, which is to say that the pronoun 'he' in 'he said' refers to al-Shafi'i, not to the author, and the intent is that al-Shafi'i mentioned his principle in the discussion of blood-money.
Source pages p. 218

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on the ruling concerning a witness in a zina case who retracts after the accused has been stoned. The passage type is a ruling with proof, incorporating both intra-madhhab and inter-madhahab disputes. The author begins by addressing Zufar's argument that no hadd is required. Zufar claimed: if the retractor slanders a living person, the hadd is dropped by death; if he slanders a dead person, the dead person was stoned by a judge's ruling, so there is doubt and the hadd is not imposed. The Hanafi response (from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad) is that the retractor indeed slanders a dead person, but because his retraction nullifies the testimony, the judge's ruling is annulled; thus the stoned person is no longer considered stoned by a valid ruling. Hence, no doubt arises, and the hadd for qadhf is imposed. The text then provides the ruling: the retracting witness must be punished with the hadd of qadhf (since he becomes a slanderer) and must pay a quarter of the diya (blood-money) for the life lost. This is the Hanafi position. The passage also compares with al-Shafi'i's view on retaliation in homicide cases: if witnesses to a murder retract after execution, al-Shafi'i requires retaliation (qisas) against them, while the Hanafi school requires only diya. The same principle is applied here, where stoning is analogous to execution. Finally, the passage clarifies a textual reference: the author of Al-Hidayah incorrectly referred to the book of diyat; the correct reference is the book of shahada where the issue is discussed.

Key Terms
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina (unlawful sexual intercourse) against a chaste person.
دية (diya): Blood-money, financial compensation paid for unlawful killing or injury.
مرجوم (marjum): A person who has been stoned to death as a punishment for zina.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction, withdrawal of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what happens to a witness who retracts after the accused in a zina case has been stoned?
A) The witness is subject to hadd qadhf and must pay a quarter of the diya.
B) The witness is subject to retaliation (qisas) by the heirs of the deceased.
C) The witness is not punished because of doubt (shubha).
D) The witness is only required to pay a fine but not subjected to hadd.

Key Takeaway
A retracting witness in a zina case must receive hadd qadhf and pay a quarter of diya, reflecting the Hanafi principle that false testimony leading to death requires financial compensation rather than retaliation.

Witness Retraction Before Stoning in Zina Cases
Explains Hanafi ruling when witness retracts before stoning is carried out

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on witness retraction in a zina case before stoning and identify the conditions that trigger the hadd of qadhf.

Core Idea
Retraction before stoning invalidates testimony; witnesses are punished for qadhf, not the accused.

This lesson examines a specific ruling within the Hanafi law of hudud: what happens when one of the four witnesses in a zina case retracts before the accused is stoned. The passage clarifies that retraction nullifies the testimony, so the accused goes free, but the witnesses are liable for the hadd of false accusation (qadhf). This ruling underscores the importance of certainty in hudud cases and the protection of the accused from baseless punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Four witnesses testify to zina against a man who is muhsan (eligible for stoning). Before the stoning is carried out, one witness retracts.
Retraction may occur after the judge's verdict but before execution.
2
Determine the effect on the accused
The retraction creates doubt (shubha), so the hadd of zina is not enforced. The accused is released without punishment.
Hudud are suspended by doubt.
3
Determine the effect on the witnesses
All four witnesses are subjected to the hadd of qadhf (eighty lashes) because their testimony was false, as shown by the retraction.
The retraction retroactively proves false testimony.
4
Understand the timing condition
The ruling applies as long as stoning has not been carried out. After stoning, retraction is not accepted and does not affect the punishment.
The passage only addresses retraction before stoning.
5
Grasp the underlying principle
Certainty cannot be overridden by doubt, but here the retraction itself creates doubt about the original certainty, so the hudud punishment is avoided, but the false accusers are still punished to protect societal integrity.
This balances the rights of the accused and the community.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقبله حدُّوا فقط) : أي رجع من الأربعة حد جميعُ الشُّهودِ حد القذف، ولا يحد المشهود عليه
[٤]قوله : وقبله ؛ يعني لو شهدوا بالزّنى على رجل وهو محصن ولم يرجم حتى رجع واحد منهم عن شهادته، سواء كان ذلك بعد قضاء القاضي بالرجم أو بعده أقيمَ حد القذف على الجميع لا على المشهود به ؛ لعدم ثبوت الزني.
'And before that they are only subject to hadd' – meaning if one of the four retracts, all witnesses are subjected to the hadd of slander, and the accused is not subjected to hadd. [4] His statement: 'And before that'; meaning if they testified to zina against a man who is muhsan and he has not been stoned until one of them retracts from his testimony, whether that is after the judge's ruling of stoning or after it, the hadd of slander is established on all of them, not on the accused, because zina has not been established.
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage is a straightforward ruling statement dealing with the scenario where witnesses in a zina case retract before the accused has been stoned. The ruling is that all witnesses are subjected to the hadd of qadhf (slander) because their retraction reveals that they falsely accused a chaste person. The accused is not punished because the testimony was not sustained, so the charge of zina is not proven. This applies whether the retraction occurs after the judge's verdict but before the actual stoning, or earlier. The key point is that as long as the stoning has not been carried out, the retraction invalidates the evidence, and the witnesses become liable for hadd qadhf.

Key Terms
إحصان (ihsan): The status of being a free, adult, married Muslim who has consummated a valid marriage, making stoning the punishment for zina.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment for falsely accusing a chaste person of zina: eighty lashes.
رجوع (ruju'): Retraction; the act of a witness withdrawing their testimony before the punishment is carried out.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If four witnesses testify to zina against a muhsan man, but one retracts before the stoning is carried out, what is the ruling?
A) All witnesses are punished for qadhf, and the accused is also stoned.
B) Only the retracting witness is punished for qadhf, and the accused is freed.
C) All witnesses are punished for qadhf, and the accused is not punished.
D) No one is punished because the testimony is incomplete.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, retraction by any witness before the execution of stoning invalidates the entire testimony, freeing the accused and making all witnesses liable for the hadd of false accusation.

Retraction of Zina Testimony: Hanafi Rulings and Intra-Madhhab Disputes
Expansion of rulings on retraction of zina testimony

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling when one of four zina witnesses retracts, identify the intra-Hanafi differences (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, Zufar), and compare with the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
When a zina witness retracts, their testimony becomes slander — all witnesses may be flogged, and the retractor pays diyah.

This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah expands on the consequences of retraction in zina testimony. The core Hanafi position is that retraction nullifies the testimony and reveals it as slander, leading to the hadd of qadhf for all witnesses and partial diyah for the retractor. However, there are nuanced disagreements within the Hanafi school regarding timing and the effect of judgment. We will unpack these positions and the reasoning behind the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic ruling
State the ruling when one of the four witnesses retracts before punishment: all witnesses are flogged for qadhf and the retractor pays a quarter of diyah.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa and the relied-upon view.
2
Understand the timing distinction
Note the difference between retraction before and after the judge's ruling. The text discusses whether the judgment strengthens the testimony.
Imam Muhammad holds that retraction after judgment only affects the retractor.
3
Examine intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Zufar. Abu Hanifa: all flogged regardless. Muhammad: only retractor flogged if after judgment. Zufar: only retractor if before judgment.
The conflict centers on whether the original testimony is slander or becomes testimony by judgment.
4
Compare with Shafi'i
Contrast the Hanafi position on retraction in qisas cases with al-Shafi'i. Hanafis impose diyah; Shafi'is apply retaliation.
The difference stems from whether retraction changes the nature of the act to slander.
5
Apply the tarjih
Determine the mufta bihi: the position of Abu Hanifa (all flogged) is relied upon, as supported by al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah.
This is because the original speech is qadhf unless upheld by judgment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحدود باب شهادة الزنا والرجوع عنها
وغرِمَ رُبعَ الدِّية ، وقبلَهُ حدُّوا فقط
وغَرِمَ رُبعَ الدّية : هذا عندنا، وعند الشافعي له يقتص بناءً على أصله في شهودِ القصاص، كما قال في الديات.
وقبله حدُّوا فقط : أي رجع من الأربعة حد جميعُ الشُّهودِ حد القذف، ولا يحد المشهود عليه. وفيه قوله : وغرم؛ أي وجب على الراجع أن يضمن ربع دية النفس، فإن رجعوا كلهم وجبت عليهم الدية كاملة. وقوله : بناءً على أصله... الخ؛ فإنّ شهود القتل عمداً الموجب للقصاص إذا رجعوا بعدما قتل المشهود عليه، فعند الشافعي يجب عليهم القصاص، وعندنا الدية، فكذا هاهنا فإنّ الرجم في حكم القتل. وقوله : كما قال في الديات؛ ظاهره أنّ هذه المسألة ذكرها المصنف في بحث الديات، وهو حوالة غير صحيحة، فإنّه لا أثر لهذه المسألة لا في المتن ولا في الشرح في «كتاب الديات»، نعم لها ذكر في «كتاب الشهادة» في «فصل منعقد لذكر مسائل الرجوع عنها»، حيث قال المصنف له هناك : «وفي القصاص الدية فقط»، وقال الشارح : «أي إذا شهدا أنّ زيداً قتل عمراً فاقتص زيد، ثم رجعا تجب الدية عندنا، وعند الشافعي له يقتص». انتهى. وقد وقع الخطأ في هذا المقام عن صاحب الهداية في الحوالة إلى «كتاب الديات» أيضاً، فطالعها إن شئت. ولنا : توجيه يحفظ به كلام الشارح هاهنا الخطأ، وهو أن يقال : ضمير قال عن راجع إلى الشافعي له لا إلى المصنّف، ويكون المقصود أنّ الشافعي ذكر أصله المذكور في بحث الديات. وقوله : وقبله؛ يعني لو شهدوا بالزّنى على رجل وهو محصن ولم يرجم حتى رجع واحد منهم عن شهادته، سواء كان ذلك بعد قضاء القاضي بالرجم أو بعده أقيمَ حد القذف على الجميع لا على المشهود به؛ لعدم ثبوت الزني.
ثم: ولا شيء على خامس رجع، فإن رجع آخر حدا، وغرما
فإن كان الرّجوع بعد الحكم، فعند محمد الله حدَّ الرَّاجع فقط، ولا يحد الباقون؛ لتأكد شهادتهم بالقضاء.
قلنا: القضاء ينفسخ وإن كان الرجوع قبل الحكم، فعند زفر له حد الراجع فقط.
وقوله: حد الراجع فقط؛ لأنّ الشهادة تأكدت بقضاء القاضي بالرجم، فلا تنفسخُ إلا في حق الراجع، كما إذا رجع واحد بعد إمضاء الحد على ما مر، وبهذا التقرير الذي ذكره في «الهداية» وغيرها يظهرُ أنه لا يفيد ما ذكره الشارح له في الجواب من قبلهما : إنّه انفسخ القضاء، يعني لما رجع الشاهد انفسخ القضاء بالرجم، فلم يوجد تأكد شهادتهم بالقضاء؛ وذلك لأنّ محمداً لله لا ينكر انفساخ القضاء، وإنما يجعل الانفساخ مقتصراً في حق الراجع. وقد أجاب صاحب «الهداية» من قبلهما بما توضيحه : إنّ إمضاء الحدّ أيضاً من القضاء، فرجوعه قبل الإمضاء رجوع قبل القضاء، وفي الرجوع قبل القضاء يُحدُّ الكل عند محمد له أيضاً، فكذا هاهنا.
وقوله: حد الراجع فقط؛ لأنه صار قاذفاً بالرجوع، ولا يُصدق على غيره، فلا يحد غيره برجوعه. ونحن نقول: إن كلامهم في الأصل قذف صريح، وإنما يصير شهادة باتصال فإذا لم يتصل به القضاء بقي قذفاً فيحدون جميعاً.
وقوله: ولا شيء؛ يعني إن شَهِدَ خمسة رجال بزنى رجل ثم رجع بعد واحد منهم لا يجب شيء على الأربعة، لا الدية ولا الحدّ؛ لأنه بقي من يبقى بشهادته كل الحق، وهو شهادة الأربعة.
وقوله: حدا؛ أي الراجعان حد القذف؛ لأنه لم يبق من الشهودِ مَن يتم به الحجة، وانفسخت الشهادة في حقهما بالرجوع، فيحدّان كما مرّ.
وقوله: وغُرما؛ أي وجب على الراجعين ربع دية المرجوم؛ لأنه بقي من يبقى بشهادته...
Book of Hudud, Chapter on Testimony of Adultery and Retraction Therefrom
And he incurs a quarter of the blood-money, and before it they are only flogged.
'And he incurs a quarter of the blood-money': This is according to us. According to al-Shafi'i, he may be subjected to retaliation based on his principle regarding witnesses of retaliation, as he said in the Book of Diyat.
'And before it they are only flogged': That is, if one of the four retracts, all witnesses are flogged with the hadd of qadhf, and the person testified against is not flogged.
[Commentary: The statement 'And he incurs' means that it is obligatory for the retractor to guarantee a quarter of the blood-money of the person; if all retract, the full blood-money is incumbent upon them. The statement 'based on his principle' etc.: For if witnesses of intentional killing requiring retaliation retract after the defendant has been executed, according to al-Shafi'i they are subject to retaliation, while according to us they pay blood-money. Similarly here, since stoning is in the category of killing. The statement 'as he said in the Book of Diyat': Apparently, the author mentioned this issue in the discussion of diyat, but this reference is incorrect, for this issue has no mention in the text or commentary in the Book of Diyat. Rather, it is mentioned in the Book of Testimony, in the chapter devoted to issues of retraction, where the author said: 'In cases of retaliation, only blood-money applies,' and the commentator said: 'That is, if two testify that Zaid killed Amr, and Zaid is executed, then they retract, blood-money is obligatory according to us, while according to al-Shafi'i they may be executed.' End. An error occurred here by the author of al-Hidayah in referring to the Book of Diyat as well; consult it if you wish. We have an interpretation to preserve the commentator's words here from error, which is to say: the pronoun 'he said' refers back to al-Shafi'i, not to the author, and the intent is that al-Shafi'i stated his principle mentioned in the discussion of diyat. The statement 'and before it': It means if they testify for adultery against a man who is muhsan and he has not been stoned, and one of them retracts his testimony, whether that is after the judge's judgment of stoning or after it, the hadd of qadhf is imposed on all witnesses, not on the person testified against, due to the non-establishment of adultery.
Then: 'And nothing is on a fifth retractor, but if another retracts, they are flogged and incur [compensation].'
If retraction occurs after the judgment, then according to Muhammad there is flogging only for the retractor, and the rest are not flogged, because their testimony is strengthened by the judgment.
We say: The judgment is annulled. And if retraction occurs before judgment, then according to Zufar only the retractor is flogged.
His statement: 'Flogging only for the retractor' because the testimony is strengthened by the judge's judgment of stoning, so it is not annulled except in respect of the retractor, just as when one retracts after the execution of the hadd as has passed. And by this explanation given in al-Hidayah and others, it appears that what the commentator said in response from them—that the judgment is annulled—is not useful; meaning when the witness retracts, the judgment of stoning is annulled, so there is no strengthening of their testimony by judgment. This is because Muhammad does not deny the annulment of the judgment; rather he makes the annulment limited to the retractor. The author of al-Hidayah responded from them with clarification: The execution of the hadd is also part of the judgment, so his retraction before execution is retraction before judgment, and in case of retraction before judgment, all are flogged according to Muhammad as well; so likewise here.
His statement: 'Flogging only for the retractor' because he becomes a slanderer by retraction, and he is not believed against others, so others are not flogged due to his retraction. We say: Their speech is originally explicit slander, and it becomes testimony only by connection; if it is not connected to judgment, it remains slander, so they are all flogged.
His statement: 'And nothing' means if five men testify of a man's adultery, then one of them retracts, nothing is obligatory upon the four—neither blood-money nor hadd—because there remains those whose testimony establishes the entire right, which is the testimony of four.
His statement: 'They are flogged' means the two retractors receive the hadd of qadhf, because there remains none of the witnesses by whom the proof is completed, and the testimony is annulled with respect to both by retraction, so they are flogged as earlier.
His statement: 'And they incur' means it is obligatory for the two retractors a quarter of the blood-money of the stoned person, because there remains...
Source pages p. 219

Commentary
This passage from 'Umdat al-Ri'ayah is an expansion of the rulings on retraction of testimony in zina cases. The author begins by stating the rule: if one of the four witnesses retracts before the punishment is carried out, all witnesses are flogged with the hadd of qadhf (slander), and the defendant is not punished. The retracting witness must also pay a quarter of the diyah (blood-money) of the accused. This is the Hanafi position, and a contrast with al-Shafi'i is drawn: in cases of qisas (retaliation), al-Shafi'i would apply retaliation to retracting witnesses, whereas Hanafis replace it with diyah. The commentator clarifies that this issue is actually found in the Book of Testimony, not the Book of Diyat, and corrects a reference error in al-Hidayah. He then discusses intra-Hanafi differences: according to Imam Muhammad, if retraction occurs after the judge's ruling but before execution, only the retracting witness is flogged because the testimony is strengthened by the ruling. However, the commentator points out that the ruling itself is annulled by the retraction. Zufar holds that even if retraction occurs before the ruling, only the retractor is flogged, but the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and others) is that all witnesses are flogged because their original speech is slander, and it only becomes valid testimony if upheld by judgment. The passage also covers a scenario with a fifth witness: if four witnesses testify and a fifth also testifies, retraction by one of the four within the initial set leaves the others unaffected; but if two retract, they are flogged and must pay a quarter of the diyah each, as the testimony of the remaining two is insufficient to prove adultery.

Key Terms
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The prescribed punishment of flogging for false accusation of adultery or slander, typically 80 lashes.
دية (diyah): Blood-money paid as compensation for homicide or bodily harm, paid by the retracting witnesses in this context.
رجم (rajm): Stoning to death as punishment for adultery for a muhsan (married free person).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi law, if one of the four witnesses to adultery retracts before the punishment is carried out, what happens to the witnesses?
A) Only the retracting witness is flogged for qadhf.
B) All four witnesses are flogged for qadhf, and the retractor pays a quarter of the diyah.
C) The witnesses are not flogged but must pay diyah.
D) The retractor is executed.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that retraction of zina testimony nullifies the entire testimony, transforming it into slander, so all witnesses are flogged and the retractor pays partial blood-money.

Retraction of Testimony in Zina Cases: Timing, Liability, and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Rulings on retraction of witnesses and liability for diyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on retraction of testimony in zina cases, distinguishing between retraction before and after judgment and calculating diya liability among witnesses.

Core Idea
Retraction of testimony in zina cases triggers hadd and diya, but the ruling depends on timing and the number of witnesses remaining.

This lesson examines the consequences when witnesses in a zina case withdraw their testimony. The Hanafi school applies different rules depending on whether the retraction occurs before or after the judge's verdict, and also considers how many witnesses remain to sustain the proof. Understanding these distinctions is critical for accurately applying hudud and compensating wrongful stoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the timing of retraction
Determine whether the retraction occurs before or after the judge's judgment (hukm). This is the primary factor that changes the ruling.
After judgment, the testimony is considered confirmed; before judgment, it remains mere accusation.
2
Apply the ruling for retraction after judgment
According to Imam Muhammad, only the retracting witness is punished with hadd al-qadhf; the others are not punished because their testimony was confirmed by the judgment.
The judgment is annulled only in respect of the retractor, not the others.
3
Apply the ruling for retraction before judgment and note the ikhtilaf
Zufar holds that only the retractor is punished; Muhammad holds that all witnesses are punished because their statements are considered slander until connected to judgment.
The mufta bihi is Muhammad's view: all are punished before judgment.
4
Assess the number of witnesses remaining
If fewer than four remain after retraction, the proof of zina collapses. The retractors are punished and must pay diya proportionally based on the number of witnesses who did not retract.
Principle: consideration is given to those who remain, not those who retract.
5
Extend to liability of third parties (killer and voucher)
If a person kills the accused (by means other than stoning) or vouches for witnesses who turn out to be invalid, they are liable for diya. Qiyas would require qisas, but istihsan applies due to apparent validity of judgment.
If killed by stoning (the proper method), no liability.

فإن كان الرجوع بعد الحكم، فعند محمد لا حدَّ الرَّاجع فقط ، ولا يحد الباقون ؛ لتأكد شهادتهم بالقضاء. قلنا : القضاء ينفسخ. وإن كان الرجوع قبل الحكم ، فعند زفر له حد الراجع فقط. ولا شيء على خامس رجع ، فإن رجع آخر حدا، وغرما. 
قوله : حد الراجع فقط ؛ لأنّ الشهادة تأكدت بقضاء القاضي بالرجم، فلا تنفسخُ إلا في حق الراجع، كما إذا رجع واحد بعد إمضاء الحد على ما مر، وبهذا التقرير الذي ذكره في «الهداية» وغيرها يظهرُ أنه لا يفيد ما ذكره الشارح له في الجواب من قبلهما : إنّه انفسخ القضاء، يعني لما رجع الشاهد انفسخ القضاء بالرجم، فلم يوجد تأكد شهادتهم بالقضاء ؛ وذلك لأنّ محمداً لا ينكر انفساخ القضاء، وإنما يجعل الانفساخ مقتصراً في حق الراجع. وقد أجاب صاحب «الهداية» من قبلهما بما توضيحه : إنّ إمضاء الحدّ أيضاً من القضاء، فرجوعه قبل الإمضاء رجوع قبل القضاء ، وفي الرجوع قبل القضاء يُحدُّ الكل عند محمد أيضاً، فكذا هاهنا. 
قوله : حد الراجع فقط ؛ لأنه صار قاذفاً بالرجوع، ولا يُصدق على غيره، فلا يحد غيره برجوعه. ونحن نقول : إن كلامهم في الأصل قذف صريح ، وإنما يصير شهادة باتصال فإذا لم يتصل به القضاء بقي قذفاً فيحدون جميعاً. 
قوله : ولا شيء ؛ يعني إن شَهِدَ خمسة رجال بزنى رجل ثم رجع بعد واحد منهم لا يجب شيء على الأربعة، لا الدية ولا الحدّ ؛ لأنه بقي من يبقى بشهادته كل الحق، وهو شهادة الأربعة. 
قوله : حدا ؛ أي الراجعان حد القذف ؛ لأنه لم يبق من الشهودِ مَن يتم به رجمه الحجة، وانفسخت الشهادة في حقهما بالرجوع، فيحدّان كما مرّ. 
قوله : وغُرما ؛ أي وجب على الراجعين ربع دية المرجوم ؛ لأنه بقي من يبقى بشهادته ثلاثة أرباع الحق، وهم ثلاثة شهود، وأصله أنّ المعتبر في باب الشهادة والرجوع بقاء من بقي لا رجوع من رجع على ما يأتي تفصيله إن شاء الله في «كتاب الشهادة». 
قوله : ربع ديته ؛ فإن رَجَعَ الثالث ضمن الربع وحـد، ولو رجع الخمسة غرموا كل الدية أخماساً وحدّوا جميعاً. كذا في «النهر». 
قوله : بعد الرجم ؛ وأما الرجوع قبل الرجم فقد مر أنه يسقط عنه الرجم إذا لم يبق نصاب الشهادة وحدّ حد القذف كل من رجع. 
وضَمِنَ الدِّيَةَ مَن قتل المأمور برجمه، أو زكى شهودَ الزِّنا فرجم، فظهروا عبيداً، أو كفاراً فيهما. 
قوله : من قتل... الخ ؛ يعني إذا شَهِدَ أربعة على رجل بالزني فأمر القاضي برجمه، فضرب رجل آخر عنقه، ثمّ علم أن الشهود كانوا عبيداً أو كفاراً فعلى القاتل الدية، والقياس أن يجب القصاص ؛ لأنه قتل نفساً معصومة بغير حق. ووجه الاستحسان : إنّ القضاء بالرجم صحيح ظاهراً عند القتل، فأورث ذلك شبهة أسقطت القصاص، فإن قتله قبل القضاء وجب القصاص. كذا في «الهداية». 
قوله : بطريق آخر ؛ فإن قتله بذلك الطريق ؛ أي الرجم فلا شيء عليه. 
قوله : أو زكّى ؛ ماض من التزكية، وهو معطوف على قتل، وهي عبارة عن وصف الشهود بأنهم أهل للشهادة. والحاصل : أنه شهد أربعة بزنى على رجل، وزكّى المزكي الشهود فأمر القاضي برجمه فرجمَ ثمَّ ظهر أنهم عبيد أو كفّار، فعلى المزكي الدية.
If the retraction is after the judgment, then according to Muhammad, only the retractor is punished (hadd), and the rest are not punished because their testimony was confirmed by the judgment. We say: the judgment is annulled. And if the retraction is before the judgment, then according to Zufar, only the retractor is punished. And nothing is [required] from a fifth [witness] who retracts; if another retracts, they are punished (hadd) and compensate (diya). His statement: 'only the retractor is punished' because the testimony was confirmed by the judge's verdict of stoning, so it is not annulled except regarding the retractor, just as if one retracts after the execution of the hadd as previously mentioned. And with this explanation given in Al-Hidayah and others, it becomes clear that it does not benefit what the commentator mentioned in the response from both of them: that the judgment is annulled, meaning when the witness retracted, the judgment of stoning was annulled, so their testimony was not confirmed by the judgment. And that is because Muhammad does not deny the annulment of the judgment; rather, he makes the annulment limited to the right of the retractor. And the author of Al-Hidayah responded on behalf of both of them with an explanation: that the execution of the hadd is also part of the judgment, so his retraction before execution is a retraction before judgment, and in retraction before judgment, all are punished according to Muhammad as well, so likewise here. His statement: 'only the retractor is punished' because he becomes a slanderer by retracting, and he is not believed against others, so others are not punished by his retraction. And we say: their speech originally is explicit slander, and it only becomes testimony by connection [to judgment], so if judgment is not connected, it remains slander, so all are punished. His statement: 'And nothing' means if five men testify to a man's zina, then one of them retracts, nothing is required from the four, neither diya nor hadd, because there remains with his testimony the full right, which is the testimony of four. His statement: 'they are punished' means the two retractors [receive] the hadd of slander because there does not remain among the witnesses those by whom the proof of stoning is completed, and the testimony is annulled regarding them by retraction, so they are punished as previously. His statement: 'and compensate' means upon the two retractors is incumbent a quarter of the diya of the stoned person, because there remains with his testimony three-quarters of the right, and they are three witnesses. And the principle is that in the chapter of testimony and retraction, consideration is given to those who remain, not to those who retract, as will come in detail in the Book of Testimony, God willing. His statement: 'a quarter of his diya' means if the third retracts, he guarantees a quarter and is punished, and if all five retract, they pay the full diya in fifths and are all punished. Thus in Al-Nahr. His statement: 'after stoning' means as for retraction before stoning, it has passed that stoning is dropped if the number of witnesses remains incomplete, and every retractor is punished with the hadd of slander. And he guarantees the diya: the one who kills the person ordered to be stoned, or who declares the witnesses of zina trustworthy and then they are stoned, and then they turn out to be slaves or disbelievers in both cases. His statement: 'the one who kills...' means if four testify to a man's zina, and the judge orders his stoning, then another man strikes his neck, then it becomes known that the witnesses were slaves or disbelievers, then upon the killer is the diya. By analogy, retaliation would be required because he killed a protected soul without right. The basis of istihsan: the judgment of stoning was apparently valid at the time of killing, so it created a doubt that removed retaliation. If he killed him before the judgment, retaliation is required. Thus in Al-Hidayah. His statement: 'by another way' means if he kills him by that way (i.e., stoning), then nothing is upon him. His statement: 'or who declares trustworthy' is past tense from tazkiyah, and it is conjoined to 'kills', and it is an expression describing the witnesses as being qualified for testimony. The summary: four testify to a man's zina, and the muzakki declares the witnesses trustworthy, so the judge orders his stoning, and he is stoned, then it becomes clear that they were slaves or disbelievers, then upon the muzakki is the diya.
Source pages p. 220

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school on the retraction of testimony in zina cases and the resulting liabilities. The text first discusses the effect of retraction after judgment: according to Imam Muhammad, only the retractor is punished with the hadd of qadhf (false accusation), while the other witnesses are not punished because their testimony was confirmed by the judge's ruling. The commentator clarifies that this is because the judgment of stoning is annulled only with respect to the retractor, not the others. He then compares this to the case of retraction before judgment, where Zufar holds that only the retractor is punished. However, the text refutes this by arguing that before judgment, the witnesses' statements are considered slander (qadhf), so all are punished. The passage then addresses a scenario with five witnesses: if only one retracts, nothing is required from the remaining four because they still form a complete proof (four witnesses needed for zina). If two retract, they are each punished and must pay a quarter of the diya (blood money) of the stoned person, because three-quarters of the proof remains (the three who did not retract). The principle is that consideration is given to those who remain, not those who retract. The text then turns to liability for diya: a person who kills the one ordered to be stoned (by a method other than stoning) is liable for diya if the witnesses later turn out to be invalid (slaves or disbelievers). The ordinary rule (qiyas) would require qisas (retaliation), but istihsan (juristic preference) applies because the judgment was apparently valid at the time, creating a doubt that removes qisas. Similarly, a person who vouches for the witnesses (tazkiyah) is liable for diya if they are later found to be unfit. The key takeaway is the subtle distinction between retraction before and after judgment, and the reliance on the principle of 'consideration of those who remain' in testimony.

Key Terms
رجوع عن الشهادة (rujūʿ ʿan al-shahādah): Withdrawal of testimony by a witness before or after judgment.
حد القذف (ḥadd al-qadhf): Punishment of 80 lashes for false accusation of zina.
دية (diyah): Blood money paid as compensation for wrongful death or injury.
تزكية (tazkiyah): Vouching for the credibility of witnesses by declaring them trustworthy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In a zina case with five witnesses, two retract before judgment. What is the liability of the two retractors?
A) Both are punished with hadd and each pays one-fifth of the diya.
B) Both are punished with hadd and each pays one-quarter of the diya.
C) Only one retractor is punished; the other is not.
D) Both are punished with hadd but no diya.

Key Takeaway
Retraction of testimony in zina cases requires careful assessment of timing and the number of remaining witnesses to determine hadd and diya liability.
